## §S199 — gaps filed S199 (2026-06-16, gap-184 / kickstarter §11.1 scope)

### G-COLON-SHORTHAND-MARKUP-MISPARSE — an engine state-child `:`-shorthand with a MARKUP body (`<Idle> : <button>…</button>`) mis-parses; the block-splitter swallows the `<engine>` and emits a misleading `E-STRUCTURAL-ELEMENT-MISPLACED` cascade — `NEW S199; MED; RESOLVED 2026-06-18 (fix direction a — §4.13 angleDepth + engine compound-lift exemption)`
An engine state-child opener using the `:`-shorthand with a MARKUP-valued body — at least the after-`>` deprecated placement (`<Idle rule=.Loading> : <button onclick=load()>Load</button>`) — confuses the block-splitter: it cannot disambiguate the state-child opener's terminating `>` from the markup body's tags, loses logic-body close tracking, and reports the WRONG diagnostic: `E-STRUCTURAL-ELEMENT-MISPLACED: <engine> cannot appear inside a ${} logic body` pointing at the `<engine>` opener, plus a cascade (`E-STATE-UNDECLARED` on the engine's auto-cell writes, `E-VARIANT-AMBIGUOUS` on bare variants). The `<engine>` is NOT in a logic body — the diagnostic blames the wrong construct. **PA-probed S199:** `/tmp/ks-111.scrml` (the kickstarter §11.1 recipe) + `/tmp/ks-111b.scrml` (same minus the redundant `${}` wrapper) both FAIL at the `<engine>` line with E-STRUCTURAL; converting the state-children to BARE-BODY (`<Idle rule=.Loading><button>…</button></>`) clears it (the modernized recipe `/tmp/ks-final.scrml` compiles exit 0). Minimal isolation: a plain `function`-then-`<engine>` with bare-body state-children compiles; the trigger is specifically the `:`-shorthand-with-markup-body. **RESOLVED 2026-06-18 (g-colon-shorthand-markup-misparse-2026-06-18) — FIX DIRECTION (a).** SPEC ruling (Rule 4): markup-as-value IS a legal `:`-shorthand single-expression body — §4.14:985 ("markup-as-value (cross-ref §1.4) are all legal as the single-expression body"), §4.14:1029 worked engine example (`<Loading rule=... : <p>Loading...</>>`), §51.0.I:25826 (state-child shorthand is a code-default single expression incl. "nested tags (markup-as-value)"), §4.14:990 ("the `angleDepth` rule (§4.13) applies inside the expression — embedded markup is handled by tracking angle depth"). The after-`>` placement is DEPRECATED but parses IDENTICALLY, surfacing only the info-level `W-COLON-SHORTHAND-LEGACY-PLACEMENT` (§4.14:999 / §51.0.I:25813 / §18.0.1:11216). "Prefer bare-body for multi-element markup arms" is a DOC NOTE (preference), NOT a prohibition → so the fix is to disambiguate, not reject. **ROOT (deeper than the gap framing — the misleading E-STRUCTURAL was a SYMPTOM, ast-builder.js was not the root):** TWO block-splitter defects. (1) `scanAttributes` tracked brace/paren/bracket/ternary depth but NOT angle depth inside a `:`-shorthand body (documented gap in its header comment), so the INSIDE-OPENER form (`<Loading : <p>x</p>>`) truncated the body at the inner `<p>`'s `>` → E-CTX-001 cascade. (2) `engine`/`machine` were MISSING from `COMPOUND_LIFT_EXEMPT_TAGS`, so a top-level `<engine>` whose state-children use the AFTER-`>` `:`-shorthand was mis-classified as a compound state-decl (the `:` after a child opener's `>` reads as a Shape-2 typed-state-decl signal in `classifyOpenerForCompoundScan`), captured as opaque text, and EOF-dissolved into a top-level text run → the engine never became a block → the misleading E-STRUCTURAL on the `<engine>` opener + the bare-variant cascade (this fired even for a NON-markup after-`>` body — body content was irrelevant; the compound-lift mis-classification was the trigger). **FIX (compiler/src/block-splitter.js, 2 commits):** (a) §4.13 angleDepth tracking in `scanAttributes` gated on `shorthand===true` (embedded markup `<tag>`/`</tag>`/`<tag/>` `>`s are body content; the opener `>` is the one at angle depth 0); (b) `COMPOUND_LIFT_EXEMPT_TAGS += engine, machine` (parallel to the match/each exemption — engine is a Tier-2 structural container per §4.15/§51.0, not a compound state-decl); (c) main-loop after-`>` recognition (`tryConsumeAfterCloseColonShorthand` + `topIsEngineBody` scope guard) routing an after-`>` engine state-child to the shorthand-leaf emit, captured verbatim into engine-decl.rulesRaw for the engine-statechild-parser re-parse + lint. ALSO fixes the canonical INSIDE-OPENER markup form (`<Loading : <p>…</p>>`), which had its own E-CTX-001 failure (the gap framing named only after-`>`). No over-relax: a GENUINE `<engine>` inside a real `${}` logic body STILL fires E-STRUCTURAL-ELEMENT-MISPLACED; E-COLON-SHORTHAND-ON-VOID + E-CLOSER-001 intact. Regression gate: `compiler/tests/unit/g-colon-shorthand-markup-misparse.test.js` (12 tests — BS-level shorthand-leaf shape + E2E compile + legacy-lint count + no-over-relax). Full suite green.
<!-- @gap id=g-colon-shorthand-markup-misparse sev=MED status=resolved -->

### G-EACH-COMPONENT-BODY-INVALID-JS — `<each>` rendering a user-COMPONENT body breaks component expansion: helpers go out of scope (E-SCOPE-001) + an internal `if=(expr is some)` emits invalid JS (E-CODEGEN-INVALID-JS) — `NEW S199; HIGH; component-body core RESOLVED S200; if=/predicate SPLIT to g-each-peritem-if-predicate-not-lowered`
A `<each in=@coll as x>` whose per-item body renders a user component (`<Card it=x/>`, `<LoadCard load=l/>`) mis-expands the component inside the each render-fn: (1) the component's own imported helpers / `fn`s go OUT OF SCOPE — `E-SCOPE-001: Undeclared identifier 'statusLabel' / 'formatRate' / 'formatPickupAt'`; (2) the component's internal `if=(field is some)` attribute is emitted raw into a JS expression — `setAttribute("if", String((load . weight_lbs is some)))` → `E-CODEGEN-INVALID-JS` ("the compiler emitted JavaScript it cannot itself parse"). The SAME component renders correctly inside the Tier-0 `${ for (x of @coll) { lift <Comp .../> } }` form (board.scrml's original compiles) — so the bug is the `<each>` per-item-render-fn EXPANSION context, NOT the component. **PA minimal repro (S199):** `/tmp/each-comp.scrml` — `<each in=@items as it><li><Card it=it/></li></each>` where `Card` is a local component with `${label(it.name)}` + `<span if=(it.note is some)>` → E-CODEGEN-INVALID-JS. **Blocks the canonical `<each>`-over-a-component-list pattern** (every list-of-cards screen) — surfaced converting the flagship trucking dispatch board (`board.scrml`, 3 `<LoadCard>` columns) from `${for lift}` to `<each>` (the conversion was REVERTED — blocked). Plain-HTML-body `<each>` (no component) compiles fine. Likely root: CE (component-expander) does not run / loses the component-import scope inside `emit-each.ts`'s per-item render function (emitted as a separate closure that doesn't carry the component scope or trigger CE the way the for-lift markup path does); may relate to the §6.3 Landing-1 "attribute-interpolation on per-item openers is best-effort" caveat. Per `feedback_dont_soft_classify_bugs`, emitting invalid JS is a BUG (not a limitation). Fix needs an `emit-each.ts` × component-expander interaction review. **COMPONENT-BODY CORE RESOLVED S200 (STEP 1 `60ace8b4` + STEP 2 A+B `ecba9fee`).** The original diagnosis was PARTLY WRONG: the for-lift form does NOT "render correctly" — it only COMPILES. R26-confirmed in happy-dom — the inlined component body's helper calls (`formatRate`/`label`) survive into the client bundle UNBOUND → a silently-swallowed runtime `ReferenceError` ("scrml effect error") + the cards never render. A LATENT bug in every shipped component-with-helper (incl. the flagship board). Root: CE inlines the component body (the helper CALLS) but never binds the helper DEFINITIONS in the consumer; the `<each>` path exposed it at compile (E-SCOPE-001) while for-lift hid it until runtime. Fixed: **(STEP 1)** when a consumer imports a component from module M, augment that import with M's non-component (helper) exports; **(STEP 2-A)** for TRANSITIVELY-inlined modules the consumer never imports (nested `<LoadStatusBadge>` → `statusLabel`), synthesize a consumer import + matching importGraph edge, injected into an import-bearing logic block (TS scope) + ast.imports/importGraph (codegen key); **(STEP 2-B)** `buildPropExprMap`/`substituteProps` now substitute EXPRESSION-valued nested props (call-ref `s=fmt(n)` / member `status=load.status`) that previously dropped → bare leak. Regression gates: `g-each-component-helper-hoist` + `g-each-component-transitive-helper` browser tests; full suite 24,377/0. **REMAINING (split to its own gap):** the board's `<each>` conversion still hits `E-CODEGEN-INVALID-JS` on LoadCard's `if=(load.weight_lbs is some)` — a SEPARATE, GENERAL each-render bug (reproduces with NO component) → `g-each-peritem-if-predicate-not-lowered`.
<!-- @gap id=g-each-component-body-invalid-js sev=HIGH status=resolved -->

### G-EACH-PERITEM-IF-PREDICATE-NOT-LOWERED — the `<each>` per-item codegen is a text-based emitter that never lowers `is some`/`is not`/`not` predicates (C1) AND has no `if=` conditional support (C2); both emit invalid JS — `NEW S200; HIGH; RESOLVED S200 (C1+C2, commit 39bd061f)`
The `<each>` per-item render path (`compiler/src/codegen/emit-each.ts`) builds DOM imperatively via TEXT rewriting (`rewriteIterValueExpr`: `@.field`→iterVar, `@cell`→reactive-get) and BYPASSES the structured expression emitter (`emitStringFromTree` / `parseExprToNode` + the §42 absence-predicate pipeline) the normal markup path uses. Two consequences, both `E-CODEGEN-INVALID-JS`, both reproduce with NO component:
**(C1) No predicate lowering.** `<each in=@nums as x><li>${x is some}</li></each>` emits `String((x is some))` → invalid JS. `is some` / `is not` / `is not not` / `not` are never lowered to their `__scrml_is_*__` / null-check forms in the each path; any §42 absence predicate (or `.Variant` / `T.Variant`) inside an `<each>` per-item expr breaks.
**(C2) No `if=` conditional.** `renderTemplateAttrToJs` (emit-each ~602) handles `class:` + events + interpolation/literals (the each-attr "Landing 2" scope) but DEFERS structural directives; `if=` falls through to `setAttribute("if", String((x is some)))` instead of conditionally rendering the element. The normal path lowers `if=` via the binding-registry / `isConditionalDisplay` mount-toggle (emit-variant-guard); the each per-item factory has no equivalent.
**Minimal repros:** C1 `<each in=@nums as x><li>${x is some}</li></each>`; C2 `<each in=@nums as x><em if=(x is some)>has</em></each>` — both `E-CODEGEN-INVALID-JS`. **Blocks the flagship board's `<each>` conversion** (LoadCard's `<span if=(load.weight_lbs is some)>`) even after `g-each-component-body-invalid-js`'s component-body core was fixed (STEP 1 + 2A+B cleared the scope errors; this is the remaining E-CODEGEN). **Fix direction:** route the each per-item expr emission (interpolations + attrs + the `if=` predicate) through the structured emitter (`parseExprToNode` → `emitStringFromTree`, preserving iter-scope binding) so the §42 predicate pipeline runs; add a per-item conditional that lowers the `if=` predicate + gates the element's `appendChild` (the each render-fn re-runs on collection change, so the conditional re-evaluates reactively). This is the each-render "Landing 3" — the recurring "each per-item path is a separate, incomplete emitter" class (cf. sibling `g-each-body-bare-variant-arg`, the bare-variant lowering missing in the same path). **RESOLVED S200 (C1+C2, commit 39bd061f).** New `lowerEachExpr` helper (emit-each.ts) routes per-item interpolations + setAttribute exprs through the structured emitter when a §42 predicate is present (`is some` → `(v !== null && v !== undefined)`); `if=` is now detected on the per-item element + its append GATED on the lowered predicate (`if (cond) frag.appendChild(el)`, re-evaluated per render). Regression gate `compiler/tests/browser/g-each-peritem-if-predicate.browser.test.js` (5/5 fail pre-fix); full suite 24,386/0. The board's `<each>` conversion now COMPILES end-to-end. **REMAINING for the board to RENDER correctly:** a separate, pre-existing nested-component-inlining bug → `g-nested-component-member-arg-misparse`.
<!-- @gap id=g-each-peritem-if-predicate-not-lowered sev=HIGH status=resolved -->

### G-NESTED-COMPONENT-MEMBER-ARG-MISPARSE — a member-access ARGUMENT to a NESTED component (`<Badge s=row.name/>` / `<LoadStatusBadge status=load.status/>`) mishandles the `.field` (splits to a phantom attr / drops the member); the inlined component-root class-attr interpolation also emits raw — `NEW S200; HIGH; member-arg leg RESOLVED S200 (PA-direct); case-c SPLIT → g-inlined-component-root-class-interp-raw`
When a component renders ANOTHER component and passes a MEMBER-ACCESS prop value, the `.field` is mishandled at the attr-value boundary: `<Badge s=row.name/>` parses as `s=row` + a phantom bare `name` attribute → `E-COMPONENT-011: Prop \`name\` is not declared in \`Badge\``. In the trucking board's `<LoadStatusBadge status=load.status/>` the related symptom is the member DROPPED — the inlined badge body emits `statusLabel(l)` (the whole each-iter row) instead of `statusLabel(l.status)`. ALSO surfaced: the inlined component-root class interpolation (`class="… ${statusBadgeClasses(status)}"`) is emitted RAW (the `${…}` not processed) → a literal `${…}` in the class string. **Isolation (S200):** a DIRECT component USING a member-access on its OWN prop compiles + lowers fine (`Card(row) { ${row.name} }` → `String(r.name)`); the bug is specifically the member-access ARG to a NESTED `<Comp prop=obj.field/>`. Affects BOTH the Tier-0 `${for…lift}` and `<each>` paths (NOT each-specific) — surfaced finishing the board's `<each>` conversion after `g-each-component-body-invalid-js` (A+B) + `g-each-peritem-if-predicate` (C1+C2) cleared the scope + codegen errors; the board now COMPILES but the badge renders wrong on the client (consistent with the for-lift-latently-broken finding). **Repros:** `<Badge s=row.name/>` (E-COMPONENT-011); the board's `<LoadStatusBadge status=load.status/>` (statusLabel(l) + raw class interp). **Needs:** an attr-value parse / CE prop-substitution review of member-access (`obj.field`) nested-component arguments + the inlined-root class-attr interpolation — likely the block-splitter / attr tokenizer splitting `obj.field` at the `.`; cross-ref the §6.3 "attribute-interpolation on per-item openers is best-effort" caveat. **RESOLVED S200 (PA-direct, member-access leg).** Root (NOT the attr tokenizer — its char-class already includes `.`): the LOGIC tokenizer space-pads the `.` member operator, so a component-BODY nested-component prop arg `<Badge s=row.name/>` round-trips as `s=row . name`; CE's `normalizeComponentBodyRaw` collapsed call-form (`fn ( x )`→`fn(x)`) + the `@.`-each-sigil (`@ . id`→`@.id`) but NOT a GENERAL member-access. The markup attr tokenizer (tokenizer.ts ~654) then read `row` (ATTR_IDENT stops at the space) + stranded `.name` → phantom bare attr (E-COMPONENT-011) or, when the stranded segment matched a declared prop, the silent member-DROP (`status=load.status`→`status=load`). Fix: added a general member-access collapse `obj . field`→`obj.field` in `normalizeComponentBodyRaw` (mirrors the existing call-form + `@.` collapses; chains collapse left-to-right; post-`.` letter-class so numerics/bare-variants never match). Scope: component-body-only — a top-level `${for…lift}` nested-component arg was never affected (v4 probe compiled clean). Spec: NO change — §5.2 already sanctions `obj.prop` as an atomic unquoted reference (cluster-A's reject message names it). Regression: `compiler/tests/unit/g-nested-component-member-arg.test.js` (3 tests — single / chained `row.inner.name` / case-b member-drop `status=load.status`). PA R26 on the real board (`components/load-card.scrml` `<LoadStatusBadge status=load.status/>`): emits `statusLabel(load.status)` (member preserved; was `statusLabel(l)`), board compiles clean, emitted client JS `node --check` OK. Full suite 24,390/0; within-node not over-budget. **SPLIT: the secondary "ALSO surfaced" case-c** (the INLINED component-ROOT class-attr `${…}` interp emitted raw) is a DISTINCT root, still open → `g-inlined-component-root-class-interp-raw`.
<!-- @gap id=g-nested-component-member-arg-misparse sev=HIGH status=resolved -->
Graph: [[blocks: board-each-conversion]] (the member-arg leg was a board-render blocker; resolved S200).

### G-INLINED-COMPONENT-ROOT-CLASS-INTERP-RAW — an INLINED component's ROOT class-attr `${…}` interpolation is emitted RAW (literal `${…}` in the class string), not lowered — `NEW S200; MED; open`
When CE inlines a component whose ROOT element carries a class with a `${...}` interpolation (`const Badge = <span class="base ${cls(status)}" props={ status: string }>`), the inlined element's class is emitted with the `${...}` UNPROCESSED: `_scrml_lift_el.setAttribute("class", "base ${cls(status)}")` — valid JS (`node --check` passes) but silent-WRONG (the runtime class literally contains the text `${cls(status)}`, not the computed value). Split from `g-nested-component-member-arg-misparse` (S200): that gap's PRIMARY member-arg-misparse leg was fixed PA-direct; this secondary symptom is a SEPARATE root (the CE inlined-root class-attr codegen, NOT the member-access space-padding) and is unaffected by that fix. **NOT a board blocker:** the flagship board's `<LoadStatusBadge>` (which HAS this `${statusBadgeClasses(status)}` root-class shape) is MODULE-IMPORTED, not inlined → emitted correctly via the module path; case-c fires only when such a component is INLINED (same-file, or CE transitive inlining). **PA repro (S200):** `/tmp/g-nested-arg/v6-classinterp.scrml` — a same-file `const Badge = <span class="base ${cls(status)}" props={status}>` inlined → `setAttribute("class", "base ${cls(status)}")` raw (verified `node --check` OK + the literal `${cls` present). **Needs:** a CE inlined-root class-attr review — the inlined root's class interpolation must be lowered (string-concat / dynamic-class) the way a non-inlined (module-emitted) component root's class is. Severity MED (narrow trigger: inlined-root + class-interp; the common module-import path works); re-trigger to HIGH if a flagship hits it via inlining (e.g. a future board `<each>`-over-inlined-badge). Per `feedback_dont_soft_classify_bugs`, silent-wrong codegen is a BUG — the `node --check`-passing literal `${}` masks it. **RESOLVED S202 (same Approach-B landing — each-inline-prop-member-substitution-2026-06-17).** The inlined-root class `${...}` interp is now (a) prop-substituted (CE class-merge base sourced from the POST-substitution node; `${cls(status)}`->`${cls(l.status)}`) AND (b) lowered to a template literal by the loop markup emitters (emit-lift.js / emit-each.ts string-literal-attr `${}` lowering) — was JSON.stringify'd raw. Verified on the board + the DD case-c repro: `setAttribute("class", `pill ${cls(l.status)}`)` (computed, not literal `${}`). Shared CE/loop-emitter root with the HIGH `g-each-inline-component-prop-member-unsubstituted`.
<!-- @gap id=g-inlined-component-root-class-interp-raw sev=MED status=resolved -->
Graph: [[blocks: board-each-conversion]] [[decided-by: each-inline-component-architecture-2026-06-17 verified]] (case-c; closed by the same S202 B fix, R26-verified on the real board).

### G-EACH-INLINE-COMPONENT-PROP-MEMBER-UNSUBSTITUTED — the `<each>` path INLINES a cross-file component but does NOT substitute that component's own prop when it's used as a member-access base in a nested-component arg → `E-SCOPE-001` — `NEW S201; HIGH; open`
The `<each>`-over-a-component-list pattern (the trucking board flagship + the canonical list-of-cards screen) fails to compile when the rendered component's body renders ANOTHER (transitive) component and binds one of its OWN props as a member-access arg. The board's `<each in=@incomingLoads as l><LoadCard load=l/></each>` → inside LoadCard, `<LoadStatusBadge status=load.status/>` → **`E-SCOPE-001: identifier 'load' cannot be resolved`** (×3, one per column). **Mechanism** (from the emitted `board.client.js`): the `<each>` path **INLINES** the cross-file LoadCard into the each render-fn, whereas the Tier-0 `${for…lift}` path **MODULE-IMPORTS** it (`_scrml_modules[...]`). Module-import → `load` is LoadCard's function param → resolves → works (the shipped for-lift board renders correctly). Inline → LoadCard's body is pulled in but its prop `load` is NOT substituted in the nested member-arg `status=load.status` → `load` is undeclared in the each render-fn scope. **Surfaced + exposed by the `g-nested-component-member-arg-misparse` fix (S200):** pre-fix the nested member-arg was the silent member-DROP (`status=load.status` → `statusLabel(l)`, compiled-wrong); the member-access-collapse fix preserves `load.status`, which turned the silent-wrong into a loud `E-SCOPE-001` (strictly better — `feedback_dont_soft_classify_bugs`). **Does NOT minimally reproduce** — PA ran 5 minimal probes (each+same-file inlined · for-lift+same-file · each+cross-file · each+cross-file+root-attr-interp · each+transitive-case-c-inner) and ALL compile clean; the bug needs the board's full shape (cross-file LoadCard with a multi-prop body rendering a transitive cross-file LoadStatusBadge that itself has a case-c root-class-interp, fed off a DERIVED filtered cell with `key=@.id`). A deep/delicate each-path CE-inlining bug — fresh-arc-shaped (`feedback_repeated_dispatch_crash_pa_direct`). **Design thread (DD-worthy):** for-lift module-imports + works; each inlines + breaks — the RIGHT fix may be architectural (make the `<each>` path MODULE-IMPORT components the way for-lift does, sidestepping the whole inline-prop-substitution class) rather than patching the inline substitution. Same each-inline family as `g-each-component-body-invalid-js` (RESOLVED S200 — helpers/transitive/expr-props) + the inline-interpolation family as `g-inlined-component-root-class-interp-raw` (case-c, MED). **Blocks:** the trucking board `<each>` conversion (the S193 flagship) + the ENTIRE `<each>`-over-component-list corpus pattern. **Repro:** convert `examples/23-trucking-dispatch/pages/dispatch/board.scrml`'s 3 columns to `<each in=@incomingLoads as l><div><LoadCard load=l customerName=l.customer_name/></div><empty>…</empty></each>` + 3 derived filtered cells (the conversion was authored + reverted S201 — correct idiomatic scrml that exposes this compiler bug). **Severity HIGH** (flagship + corpus-pattern gate). **RESOLVED S202 (Approach B, change-id each-inline-prop-member-substitution-2026-06-17).** Authority: scrml-support/docs/deep-dives/each-inline-component-architecture-2026-06-17.md (DD overturned the gap-entry premise: NO component-instance model exists — for-lift INLINES too and is silently runtime-broken with the SAME bug; only the diagnostic timing differs, loud-each vs silent-for-lift). Two-layer fix: **(LAYER 1, component-expander.ts substituteProps markup-attr path)** substitute a component's own prop when it is the leading identifier of a member-access in a markup attr value — variable-ref member-name (`status=load.status`, parse->substitutePropsInExprNode structured), string-literal `${}` interp (`href="/x/${load.id}"` / root `class="pill ${cls(status)}"` via new substituteInterpSegments), expr-no-exprNode (`if=(load.weight_lbs is some)` via substitutePropsInRawExpr); class-merge base now sourced from the POST-substitution `expanded` node (was raw defNode). OUTER-FIRST walkAndExpand cascades `load`->`l` then transitive Badge `status`->`load.status`->`l.status`. **(LAYER 2, emit-lift.js + emit-each.ts)** lower `${}` interp inside a string-literal markup attr into a template literal (was JSON.stringify'd raw → shipped literal `${}`), live-keyed per item. ALSO fixed (LAYER 2 un-masked it): CE STEP-2A two-hop helper-hoist — a helper an inlined component imports from a THIRD file (`badgeColor` two hops away) now hoisted into the consumer (augment a direct import node's specifiers, else synthesize). R26 board (`examples/23-trucking-dispatch/pages/dispatch/board.scrml`): compile exit 0, node --check OK, 21 substituted-emit sites, ZERO bare unsubstituted `load`/`status` in the loop body; the `<each>` form (which fired loud E-SCOPE-001 pre-fix) compiles + renders. Regression gate: `compiler/tests/browser/g-each-inline-prop-member.browser.test.js` (10 tests — substituted-emit shape + happy-dom render of nested-component + member-arg + root-class/href interp, BOTH each + for-lift). Full suite 24412/0/225. ALSO closes the silent for-lift runtime-ReferenceError class (shared CE root) + `g-inlined-component-root-class-interp-raw` (case-c). **DEFERRED (NO-SILENT-CAPS):** the inlined component root still emits its own PROP NAMES as DOM attrs (`setAttribute("load", l)` / `("status", l.status)`) — values now CORRECTLY substituted (cosmetic only; `load` stringifies to `[object Object]` as an HTML attr), a PRE-EXISTING props-as-DOM-attrs leak, NOT a render-breaker, NOT introduced here.
<!-- @gap id=g-each-inline-component-prop-member-unsubstituted sev=HIGH status=resolved -->
Graph: [[blocks: board-each-conversion]] [[decided-by: each-inline-component-architecture-2026-06-17 verified]] (the lone open HIGH that gated the board `<each>` conversion; the DD's "for-lift module-imports + works" premise was OVERTURNED by an R26 probe — verify-before-claim).

## §S202 — gaps filed S202 (2026-06-17, L1 e2e render-map triage)

All five surfaced by the new L1 e2e render-map harness (`compiler/tests/e2e-render-map/`; DD `scrml-support/docs/deep-dives/e2e-known-failure-map-2026-06-17.md`). The map ran 438 cells / 434 apps; these are the real-gap residue after triage (the 125 fails-compile were ~all corpus-filter over-inclusion of non-app compile-probe fixtures — 0 from `examples/` — not flagship regression; pending the filter refine).

### G-EACH-OVER-ARM-PAYLOAD-BINDING-UNBOUND — an `<each>` over a match/engine arm PAYLOAD BINDING emits the binding UNBOUND in the each mount-setup scope → ReferenceError at mount — `NEW S202; HIGH; RESOLVED 2026-06-17`
A variant `.Loaded(rows)` whose arm body renders `<each>` over the payload (`rows`/`items`): the arm render fn receives the binding (`_render_Loaded(rows)`) but the each per-item mount-setup emits `const _items = rows;` in a scope WITHOUT the binding → `ReferenceError: rows is not defined` at happy-dom mount. Compiles exit 0 + `node --check` OK (silent-wrong class). **Repros (single-file):** `examples/16-remote-data.scrml` (`rows`, `<match for=ContactsPhase>` arm `.Loaded(rows)`) + `examples/29-engine-vs-flags.scrml` (`items`, `<engine for=ItemsPhase>` arm `.Loaded(items)`). ONE shared root (emitted shape identical across match-arm + engine-arm). Likely loci: `emit-each.ts` + `emit-variant-guard.ts` (thread the payload binding into the each-setup scope). RESOLVED (`each-over-arm-payload-binding-unbound-2026-06-17`): ONE shared mechanism — the each-block node is STAMPED with `armPayloadBinding` (cell name + variant tag + runtime field name) at LIFT time (emit-match `buildMatchArms` / emit-engine `buildEngineArms`, where the arm payload bindings ARE known); emit-each `emitEachBodyRenderForFile` reads the stamp and resolves the iterable from the reactive cell (`_scrml_reactive_get(cell).data[field]` gated on `.variant === tag`) instead of the bare unbound name. Both repros mount clean; render-map L1 cells (16#empty/#populated, 29#empty) flipped compiles-but-throws → renders-clean. Regression: `compiler/tests/browser/each-over-arm-payload-binding-unbound.browser.test.js`.
<!-- @gap id=g-each-over-arm-payload-binding-unbound sev=HIGH status=resolved -->
Graph: [[g-each-inline-component-prop-member-unsubstituted]] (sibling each-codegen gap; found + verified by the e2e render-map, S202 Class A).

### G-FULLSTACK-EMPTY-MOUNT-THROWS — full-stack apps throw at the no-data / empty client mount instead of degrading to a loading/empty state — `NEW S202; MED; open`
`examples/17-schema-migrations.scrml` (`{} is not iterable`), `examples/22-multifile/app.scrml`, `examples/23-trucking-dispatch/app.scrml` (server-dep destructure-from-null) compile clean but THROW at the client mount when server data is absent (the `#empty` cell), rather than rendering a loading/empty state. The trucking-dispatch BOARD (`pages/dispatch/board.scrml`) renders fine — this is the APP SHELL (`app.scrml`), a DISTINCT file. A robustness gap: an app should degrade gracefully at the data-absent mount, not throw. Partly entangled with happy-dom client-only mounting (no server); the principled read is apps should not throw on the no-data mount. Surfaced by the L1 render-map (`#empty` cells = compiles-but-throws / D1-MOUNT-THROW). **RECLASSIFIED S203 (user ruling b+c) → non-gap (NOT a compiler bug).** The throws are a full-stack app's CLIENT bundle reaching a server-only resource (`scrml:store.createSessionStore`, the `<db>` store) at a server-less happy-dom mount — partly a harness artifact (no server) and partly expected (a full-stack client legitimately needs its server). The compiler is not wrong to emit the server-binding; the render-map is wrong to mount these client-only and record a server-absence as a render bug. **Harness follow-up (NOT a compiler fix):** the render-map should either mount full-stack/`<db>` apps with a mock server/store, OR record a distinct `needs-server` cell-state separate from D1-MOUNT-THROW (so these stop polluting the bug inventory). Filed against the harness, not codegen.
<!-- @gap id=g-fullstack-empty-mount-throws sev=MED status=non-gap -->
<!-- @gap id=g-rendermap-needs-server-classification sev=LOW status=open -->
<!-- (harness follow-up from the b+c ruling: add a `needs-server` cell-state OR mock-server seeding for full-stack/`<db>` apps; LOW) -->

### G-RENDER-NULLISH-TEXT — a cell/field renders literal `undefined` text into the DOM — `NEW S202; MED; open`
`examples/03-contact-book.scrml#populated` renders literal `undefined` as a text node (S-NULLISH-TEXT); `samples/compilation-tests/gauntlet-s20-meta/meta-in-component-001.scrml` likewise. A value resolving to JS `undefined` (NOT scrml `not`) reaches `textContent`/interpolation and stringifies to `"undefined"` — silent-wrong display. The `#empty` cell of 03-contact-book renders clean (the empty-vs-populated split). **DISSOLVED S203 — NOT a codegen nullish bug; both portions root-caused, neither is codegen.** (1) **03-contact-book#populated = SEED-FIXTURE GAP** (fixed): the `Contact` struct is `{id,name,email,phone}` and the template renders `${contact.phone}`, but the harness seed only supplied `{id,name,email}` → JS `undefined` → literal "undefined". In a real run `loadContacts()` SELECTs `phone`, so no undefined — the MOCK seed was incomplete. Fixed in `compiler/tests/e2e-render-map/seed-fixtures.js` (added `phone`) + a seed-shape invariant doc; the cell now `renders-clean`. (2) **meta-in-component-001 = SAMPLE BUG:** it does `for (v of reflect(Status).variants) emit(\`${v.name}\`)`, but per SPEC §14.4.2 `.variants` is an array of variant-NAME strings, so `v` is a string and `${v.name}` is `undefined` → should be `${v}`. NOT a codegen bug. The underlying reflect()-variant-shape inconsistency is filed separately (g-reflect-variant-shape-inconsistent). Surfaced + dissolved via the L1 render-map.
<!-- @gap id=g-render-nullish-text sev=MED status=resolved -->

### G-REFLECT-VARIANT-SHAPE-INCONSISTENT — `reflect()` returns enum `.variants` with inconsistent element shape across its internal paths (string vs `{name}`) — `NEW S203; LOW; RESOLVED S211`
`compiler/src/meta-checker.ts` builds reflect's `.variants` THREE ways: line ~1463 maps to bare strings (`v => typeof v === "string" ? v : v.name`), lines ~2041/~2209 build `{name}` objects. The compile-time `^{}` `reflect(Status).variants` path returns STRINGS (matching SPEC §14.4.2 `EnumType.variants` = name strings), so a consumer writing `${v.name}` silently gets `undefined` (the meta-in-component-001 sample bug). The type annotation at meta-checker.ts:264 even admits the union (`Array<string | { name: string }>`). A consumer cannot reliably know whether `v` is a string or `{name}`. LOW: pick ONE canonical shape (strings, per §14.4.2) across all reflect paths, or document the union explicitly; surfaced S203 classifying g-render-nullish-text's meta portion. **RESOLVED S211 (sPA ss7, `2c0a9e17`):** the runtime path (`emit-logic.ts serializeTypeEntry`) now emits bare strings, union-robust over the internal `string|{name}` intermediate; flipped the one locking test (`meta-type-registry-emission.test.js`, S96 pattern). The compile-time `^{}` path was already correct. Full suite 24762/0.
<!-- @gap id=g-reflect-variant-shape-inconsistent sev=LOW status=resolved -->

### G-RAW-INTERP-CHANNEL-META-CORNERS — literal `${...}` survives into rendered text in channel / for-lift-outside-logic / meta paths (bug-3 class NOT fully closed by the S202 B fix) — `NEW S202; MED; RESOLVED S204`
S-RAW-INTERP (a literal `${x}`/`${msg}`/`${n}` in the rendered DOM) fires on `samples/compilation-tests/gauntlet-s20-channels/channel-basic-001.scrml`, `…/channel-multiple-001.scrml`, and `…/gauntlet-s19-phase2-control-flow/phase2-for-lift-outside-logic-109.scrml`. The S202 B fix (`d830ec59`) closed the `${}`-in-string-literal-attr lowering for the each/lift markup-emitter path; the SAME raw-interp class survives in channel-body + for-lift-outside-logic + meta emission paths. **REFRAMED S203 (dispatch root-caused; the id is now a misnomer) — NOT a codegen `${}`-lowering bug.** The S203 dispatch (BRIEF `g-raw-interp-channel-meta-corners-2026-06-17`) verified the canonical `${ for/lift }` forms compile PERFECTLY (no raw `${}`), so the S202 LAYER-2 lowering template does not apply. The real root: **all three fixtures OMIT the `${ }` wrapper around their for-loop** (bare `for (...) {...}` directly in a `<ul>` markup body) — which SPEC §17.4 mandates (Tier-0 iteration is `${ for/lift }`). `phase2-for-lift-outside-logic-109`'s own source comment says so. With no `${ }`, the block-splitter classifies the WHOLE `for(){}` (incl. its `${...}`) as one inert `[text]` child → emitted verbatim → the `${...}` survives. The `${}` is a SYMPTOM; the disease is **a bare control-flow keyword (`for`/`if`/`while`) leading a markup-body text run is silently accepted + shipped as raw text, with ZERO diagnostic** (`BARE_DECL_RE` ast-builder.js:410 matches only decl keywords; auto-lift fires only at §40.8 roots, not nested markup). So this is a **MISSING-DIAGNOSTIC bug** (don't-soft-classify), not a render-codegen bug. The meta path was scoped OUT (meta-in-component-001 is S-NULLISH-TEXT, a different smell — see g-render-nullish-text). **OPEN pending a DESIGN RULING (PA/user):** (a) reject+recover — fire a clear diagnostic ("iteration/control-flow must be wrapped in `${ }` per §17.4") + recover, new §34 code [SPEC-faithful; agent+PA recommend]; vs (b) tolerate — widen §40.8 auto-lift to synthesize the `${ }` for control-flow-led text in any markup body [a language-surface widening; limit-primitives caution]. The 3 fixtures are deliberately-non-canonical gauntlet probes; under (a) they become expected-error fixtures. **RESOLVED S204 — ruling (a) reject+recover (S203 user "a, dispatch it"; landed S204 as the F3 reboot-bridge's first re-attach).** New §34 code `E-CONTROL-FLOW-IN-MARKUP` (§17.4 / §7; descriptive, sibling of `E-UNQUOTED-DISPLAY-TEXT` per S111): `BARE_CONTROL_FLOW_IN_MARKUP_RE` in `ast-builder.js liftBareDeclarations` (gated `parentType === "markup"`; keyword + `\b` + `(...)` head + `{` so prose/idents like `forEach`/`for sale` never match) fires ONCE per bare `for`/`if`/`while` in a markup body and RECOVERS by dropping the raw-text emission — ships NEITHER `for(){}` NOR `${...}`. The 3 named fixtures + 3 same-disease (`gauntlet-s20-sql/sql-all-001`, `sql-in-for-loop-001`, `gauntlet-s20-validation/reactive-encoded-001`) now expected-error; e2e-render-map baseline reclassified S-RAW-INTERP → fails-compile; within-node allowlist bumped for all 6. SPEC §34 row + §17.4 normative note + 11-case regression test. PA R26 dual-verified (S138): both probes fail-compile with the diagnostic, ZERO markup-body raw-interp (the only surviving `${` is the benign generated WS template literal), canonical `${ for/lift }` clean (no false-fire).
<!-- @gap id=g-raw-interp-channel-meta-corners sev=MED status=resolved -->

### G-MOUNT-HANG-RAILS-DEV — `compile` infinite-loops at 100% CPU inside `nativeParseFile` (NOT a happy-dom mount hang) — `NEW S202; reclassified MED S211; open`
`samples/gauntlet-r18/rails-dev.scrml` — **reclassified S211 (sPA ss7 R26 finding; the original "happy-dom mount hang / 0% CPU blocked" diagnosis was WRONG on both axes).** The COMPILE infinite-loops at 100% CPU: `timeout 60 bun run compiler/src/cli.js compile samples/gauntlet-r18/rails-dev.scrml -o /tmp/x/` → exit 124, 0 output files, never reaches mount. The loop is inside **`nativeParseFile`** (the native parser), reached from the meta-eval re-parse (`meta-eval.ts:380`); rails-dev is a pure compile-time `^{}` sample with no runtime effects, so "mount hang" was never plausible. **Robustness-class → above LOW (bumped MED):** a parser that fails to terminate on malformed input can hang the whole compiler via the meta-emit re-parse path. **Re-clustered → ss4** (native-parser ingestion, NOT ss7 meta-checker/render-harness — cross-ingestion escalate-trigger). Groundwork at `docs/changes/ss7-rails-dev-hang/FINDINGS.md`: reliable repro above + 8 reduced reproducers (A/B/C/D/G/H/I/J all error cleanly with `E-META-EVAL-002`; only the full sample's block *accumulation* loops — minimal repro elusive, the full sample IS the repro). Fix target: instrument `nativeParseFile` on the full repro to find the no-forward-progress token. Needs native-parser expertise + heavy conformance verification (native parser mid-migration, S115/S162 mirror hazards).
<!-- @gap id=g-mount-hang-rails-dev sev=MED status=open -->

## §S206 — gaps filed S206 (2026-06-18, trucking slice-2 §55 validity surface)

### G-COMPOUND-FIELD-RENDER-BY-TAG-UNEXPANDED — a Shape-2 field declared as a CHILD of a Variant-C compound does NOT get its render-by-tag `<field/>` expanded; the compiler silently emits a LITERAL `<field />` tag (no input, no diagnostic) — `NEW S206; MED; RESOLVED S207`
A Shape-2 decl-coupled-with-render-spec field (`<field validators> = <input.../>`, §6.2/§55) declared as a CHILD of a Variant-C compound (`<form> <field req ...> = <input/> </>`) and referenced in markup via render-by-tag (`<field/>`) is NOT expanded to its bound input. The compiler emits a LITERAL `<field />` tag into the SSR HTML, SILENTLY (exit 0, NO diagnostic) — the input never renders. The IDENTICAL field declared at TOP LEVEL (`<field req ...> = <input/>` not nested in a compound) expands correctly to `<input ... data-scrml-render-by-tag>`. The §55 validity surface for the compound (`@compound.isValid`, per-field `.errors`, `<errors of=>`, touched) WIRES CORRECTLY — only the field's render-by-tag input ELEMENT is dropped. Per `feedback_dont_soft_classify_bugs`, a silently-dropped input element (no diagnostic, input never renders) is a BUG, not a limitation. **PA repro (S206, durable):** `docs/changes/g-compound-field-render-by-tag-unexpanded-2026-06-18/repro/compound-rbt.scrml` (compound field `<signup><uname req length(>=2)> = <input/></>` + `<uname/>` → emits literal `<uname />`) vs `repro/toplevel-rbt.scrml` (same field at top level → expands to `<input type="text" id="u" ... data-scrml-render-by-tag>`). Both compile exit 0 on HEAD `105f1ee4`; the divergence is the bug. **WORKAROUND (in-corpus S206):** render the input via raw `<input bind:value=@compound.field>` — the full bind + touched + §55 validity wiring still emits (every slice-2 trucking form uses this). Likely root: the render-by-tag expander (the path that turns `<field/>` into the field's bound `<input>`) resolves a field decl in the CURRENT scope but does not descend into Variant-C compound members, so a `<field/>` whose decl lives inside a compound is treated as an unknown element → emitted as a literal tag. Surfaced converting the flagship trucking dispatch forms to the §55 validity surface (slice-2). Fix needs a render-by-tag-expander × compound-member-scope review. **RESOLVED S207** (`9997ef11`): the render-by-tag resolver (S157 Bug-60 path in `emit-html.ts`) resolved compound members ONLY via the LEXICAL `enclosingCompoundStack` — empty when `<field/>` is referenced OUTSIDE the compound body (a sibling `<form>`), so the bare tag fell through to literal emission. Fix: NEW `symbol-table.ts lookupCompoundMembersByLeafName` (non-lexical scan of in-scope compound parents by leaf name) → exactly-one-match routes to the SAME top-level Shape-2 bound-input expansion (keyed on `signup.uname`); >1 match fires NEW fatal `E-CELL-AMBIGUOUS-MEMBER-RENDER` (§6.4, no silent pick); `dependency-graph.ts compoundMemberToParent` map credits the parent compound (clears the spurious E-DG-002). §6.3:2290 confirmed EXPAND (Rule-4). +11 tests; R26: literal→`<input data-scrml-render-by-tag>`, E-DG-002 gone, FULL suite 24522/0.
<!-- @gap id=g-compound-field-render-by-tag-unexpanded sev=MED status=resolved -->

## §S195 — gaps filed S195 (2026-06-15, corpus-rewrite wave-1a)

### G-ENGINE-AUTODECL-BARE-VARIANT-WRITE — auto-declared `<engine for=T>` (no manual `<var>` decl) + bare-variant writes in a sibling `function` body fire `E-VARIANT-AMBIGUOUS` — `NEW S195; MED; RESOLVED S205 (landed S206)`
An `<engine for=T initial=.V>` relies on PRIMER §7's auto-declared-variable promise (first engine auto-declares `<var>`). But bare-variant writes (`@var = .Variant`) in a sibling `function` body fire `E-VARIANT-AMBIGUOUS` (§14.10) — the type-checker cannot see the auto-cell's type from the function scope. The kickstarter §11.1 engine recipe VERBATIM does NOT compile (5 errors: E-STRUCTURAL-ELEMENT-MISPLACED + 2× E-STATE-UNDECLARED + 2× E-VARIANT-AMBIGUOUS). Workaround: add an explicit `<var>: T = .Initial` decl alongside the engine — which then draws `E-DG-002` "declared but never consumed." Surfaced by the 16-remote-data wave-1a grounding (the `<match for=Phase>` form has no such gap — the load-bearing reason 16 went match, not engine). Fix touches the type-system (auto-cell type visible to sibling fn-body bare-variant resolution) + the kickstarter §11.1 recipe currency. **RESOLVED S205 (R26 reverse-direction narrowed the root):** the PA-scoped WRITE path (`@var = .Variant` in a sibling fn, matching names) was ALREADY clean at the S195 gap-filing commit (BUG-2 S102 + §14.10 pos #2 via the scopeChain prior-bind lookup, type-system.ts ~9004-9024) — the kickstarter §11.1 verbatim recipe ALSO compiled clean at HEAD and at S195. The original 5-error breakdown was the 16 engine-attempt, where E-STRUCTURAL + the colon-shorthand-markup bodies are the SEPARATE `g-colon-shorthand-markup-misparse` gap (its parse cascade orphaned the engine auto-cell → the downstream E-STATE-UNDECLARED + E-VARIANT-AMBIGUOUS). The GENUINE residual root, found by probing the full path: a bare-variant at a COMPARISON position INSIDE a `return` expression in a sibling fn (`function isLoading() -> bool { return @phase == .Loading }`) fired E-VARIANT-AMBIGUOUS "position type is not an enum" — NOT engine-specific (a plain `<phase>: Phase` cell failed identically; the `if (@phase == .Idle)` form already worked). Root: the `return-stmt` case (type-system.ts visitNode ~10024) wired the return-TYPE walker (`inferBareVariantsInExpr`, S84 Gap B.3) + the call-arg walker (Gap B.4) but NOT the comparison-site pre-pass (`inferBareVariantsAtComparisonSites`) that the if/while-condition (~9786) and reactive-init (~9037) sites thread — so the bare `.Loading` was fed to the return-type walker with `-> bool` as context. Was explicitly logged OUT-OF-SCOPE in `bare-variant-binary-expr-inference.test.js`'s S84 header. SPEC ruling: §14.10 (the implicit seventh position — "any other position where the type is fixed by the surrounding declaration" — covers `@cell == .V`; engine `for=T` named as a resolving locus), §51.0.C (the engine auto-cell IS a reactive cell typed to the enum, "readable everywhere"), §7.6.1 (file-level cells reachable from any sibling fn body). Fix: add `inferBareVariantsAtComparisonSites(retExprNode, scopeChain, retSpan, errors)` to the return-stmt case BEFORE the return-type walker (the helper stamps `_bareVariantInferredAtBinaryExpr` so the contextType walker skips it — no double-fire). +10 unit tests (`engine-autodecl-bare-variant-write.test.js`); negatives still error (`return .V` direct / typo→E-TYPE-063 / union-shared→E-VARIANT-AMBIGUOUS / non-enum int cell). No `E-DG-002` workaround introduced. Kickstarter §11.1 currency: NO touch needed — the verbatim recipe (write-only) already compiles clean.
<!-- @gap id=g-engine-autodecl-bare-variant-write sev=MED status=resolved -->

### G-BLOCKSPLITTER-COMMENT-SPAN-NOT-OPAQUE — the block-splitter / arm + state-child scanners don't treat `<!-- -->` as opaque — `NEW S195; LOW; open`
Two triggers, one root (comment spans aren't exempted from scanner state-tracking): (a) an HTML comment containing literal tag-mentions (`<each>`/`<empty>`) inside a `<match>` arm body counts them toward closer balance → `E-MATCH-PARSE-001` (16-remote-data finding); (b) an ODD number of `'` inside a comment in an `<engine>` state-child body opens a phantom single-quote string that swallows the rest of the body → spurious `E-ENGINE-STATE-CHILD-MISSING` for every variant (05-multi-step-form finding). Both worked around in the wave-1a rewrites (no special chars in in-body comments). Fix: exempt `<!-- -->` spans from quote-state + tag-stack tracking in `block-splitter.js` + the arm/state-child scanners. Sibling-adjacent to the GAP-A void-scanner fix (`f563bc89`), same scanner family.
**RESOLVED S210** (ss4 item-2, merge `f65b1de9`) — root was ENGINE-only, not the titled "block-splitter / arm" scope: ss4's R4 verify-before-claim found the briefSeed over-claimed the match-arm scanner — trigger (a) [HTML comment with tag-mentions in a `<match>` arm] does NOT reproduce (match raw-body + arm-closer scan handle `<!-- -->` at every position; the sibling S196 `findArmCloser`/`findNextArmOpener` quote-fix covered that family). Trigger (b) [odd `'` in a comment in an `<engine>` state-child body → phantom string → spurious E-ENGINE-STATE-CHILD-MISSING] FIXED: `engine-statechild-parser.ts` `skipCommentOrString` + `parseEngineStateChildren` now treat `<!-- -->` opaque; +7-case test. Block-splitter itself was NOT affected (over-claim). <!-- @gap id=g-blocksplitter-comment-span-not-opaque sev=LOW status=resolved -->

### G-EACH-BODY-SIGIL-INVARIANT-CLASSIFIER — `expr-node-corpus-invariant.test.js` escape-hatch classifier has no `@.`-sigil awareness — `NEW S195; LOW; open (test-infra, not a compiler bug)`
The corpus-invariant test round-trips each example's expr-nodes through acorn and bails if >50% are ParseError "escape hatches." A bare `@.`/`@.field` interpolation in an `<each>` body (a valid scrml-native contextual sigil, §17.7.3) is not standard JS, so acorn yields a ParseError → counted as an escape hatch; a small `<each>`-heavy example trips the >50% gate. 04-live-search used the canonical `as person` alias (codegen-identical) to dodge it. Consequence: examples cannot teach the bare `@.` sigil in `<each>` bodies until the classifier whitelists `@.`-bearing bare-exprs as a recognized native form. NOT a compiler bug — a test-infra classifier blind spot; relevant to later corpus waves that want to teach `@.` (gap G5). **RESOLVED S209 (sPA ss14 item2, `34ca4f9a`):** the classifier gained an `each-sigil` category — `@.`-bearing bare-exprs (acorn's `@`-plugin only consumes `@`+ident-start, so `@.` yields ParseError) are recognized + EXCLUDED from the >50% escape-hatch gate, kept VISIBLE not silenced (parse-error 2→0, each-sigil=2, 69 pass). Examples can now teach the bare `@.` sigil in `<each>` bodies.
<!-- @gap id=g-each-body-sigil-invariant-classifier sev=LOW status=resolved -->

### G-FAILABLE-ARM-NESTED-CONSTRUCTOR-CRASH — a payload-bearing variant constructor NESTED as an arg in an `!{}` arm lowers to a string-invoked-as-function → runtime crash — `NEW S195; HIGH; open`
Inside an `!{}` (or held-error-routing) arm, `@phase = .Failed(LoadError::NotFound(id))` — a payload-bearing variant constructor used as a nested arg — lowers to `data: { err: "NotFound" ( id ) }` (a string invoked as a function) → runtime crash `"NotFound" is not a function`. The SAME nested constructor in a plain `function` body lowers correctly. Site: the `!{}` arm-body rewriter `emit-logic.ts ~520-565` (rewriteBlockBody / _emitNestedGuardedArmBody). Compiles clean → crashes at runtime on a real errors-as-states idiom. Workaround (used by the landed 09): bind the whole error and route it (`| err :> { @phase = .Failed(err); return }`) — `err` is a bound var, not a nested constructor. GATES the render-expression primitive build (any display option must consume a correctly-constructed `.Failed(err)`). Surfaced by the 09-(b) rewrite + the error-handling deep-dive (Bug 1 / H4). **RESOLVED S196 (render-expr-prereq-bugs Bucket 1):** rewrite.ts:rewriteEnumVariantAccess guarded the legacy qualified-`::` unit-variant strips with `(?!\s*\()` and collapses a surviving qualified CONSTRUCTOR CALL `Enum::Variant(args)` -> the frozen-enum member-access form `Enum.Variant(args)` (byte-identical to the plain-`function`-body control). The `::`-strip was firing on the constructor call too, dropping the type prefix. R26-verified (full compile: mangle ABSENT, node --check exit 0, runtime nested tagged-object correct); +6 full-pipeline tests.
<!-- @gap id=g-failable-arm-nested-constructor-crash sev=HIGH status=resolved -->

### G-EACH-BODY-BARE-VARIANT-ARG — a bare `.Variant` enum literal as an event-handler call-ARG directly in an `<each>` per-item body emits invalid JS — `NEW S195; HIGH; RESOLVED S201 (PA-direct)`
`<each ...><button onclick=moveTo(card.id, .InProgress)>` emits the raw leading-dot `.InProgress` instead of the enum's frozen string `"InProgress"` → `E-CODEGEN-INVALID-JS`. Triangulated (wave-2 06-kanban grounding): the bare-variant→frozen-string lowering EXISTS in the Tier-0 `${for/lift}`, static-markup, and `<match>`-arm/variant-guard paths but is MISSING in the direct each-render-fn path (`compiler/src/codegen/emit-each.ts`). NON-GATING — 3 compile-verified workarounds (factor the move into a per-direction id-only handler so the bare `.Variant` lives in a fn body [the recommended idiom]; per-card `<match for=Status>`; the Tier-0 form). Parallel to wave-1 GAP-A but non-blocking (workarounds ship today). Surfaced by the wave-2 06 grounding. **RESOLVED S201 (PA-direct).** Root confirmed: `lowerEachExpr` (emit-each.ts) only routed through the structured emitter (`parseExprToNode`→`emitExprField`, which lowers bare-variants at emit-expr.ts:295) when a §42 PREDICATE was present; a bare-variant fell to the text path → raw `.X`. AND the event-handler `call-ref` branch didn't use `lowerEachExpr` at all (used `serializeCallArgs`, iter-rewrite only). Fix (2 changes, both emit-each.ts): (1) broadened `lowerEachExpr`'s guard to also detect a bare `.Variant` (leading-dot+uppercase, member-access `card.id`/`foo().Bar`/`obj.Foo` EXCLUDED); (2) NEW `serializeCallArgsLowered` (per-arg `lowerEachExpr`) used in the NON-engine call-ref handler fallback — the engine path keeps the RAW `serializeCallArgs` callText so `.advance(.X)` variant detection (emitEngineHandlerBody) still sees the intact bare-variant. PA-verified: repro emits `moveTo(card.id, "InProgress")` + `node --check` OK; engine-in-each regression emits `_scrml_engine_advance("phase", "Active", …)` (engine path intact, NOT `advance("Active")`). +2 regression tests (`each-block.test.js` g-each-body-bare-variant-arg block); full suite 24,392/0; within-node not over-budget.
<!-- @gap id=g-each-body-bare-variant-arg sev=HIGH status=resolved -->
Graph: [[g-each-inline-component-prop-member-unsubstituted]] (sibling each-codegen gap; the 2-HIGH pass, S201).

### G-HELD-ERROR-DISPLAY — a held error variant (the errors-as-states `.Failed(err)`) cannot fire its own `renders` clause — `NEW S195; MED; RESOLVED S196 (render-expression `<render of=X/>` built)`
A variant's `renders` clause (§19.2) fires ONLY when an `<errorBoundary>` (§19.6) catches a LIVE `!`-call — never for a variant HELD in a state cell. So the canonical errors-as-states lift (`@phase = .Failed(err)`) and the auto-display surface structurally never meet; today you bridge with a re-fail shim (a smell) or duplicate the per-variant markup. **RATIFIED FIX (S195, a/c):** a NEW narrow render-expression primitive ("fire this value's `renders` contract here"), exhaustiveness-fenced (reuse §19.6.6 E-ERROR-005; compile-error if a reachable variant lacks `renders`); reuses `allVariantRenderExprs` + `emitBoundaryMarkupExpr` (firing-site + data-arg change). Keyword NOT `show` (§17.2 collision) → `render`/postfix (spec-time). **RESOLVED S196 (built; surface `<render of=X/>` per S196 user ruling).** Parser registers `<render>` as a structural element (mirror `<errors>`); typer fences via E-RENDER-NO-CLAUSE / E-RENDER-NO-OF / E-RENDER-NOT-ENUM (reuses the §19.6.6 per-variant loop); codegen reuses `allVariantRenderExprs`/`emitBoundaryMarkupExpr` against the HELD value's `.data`, sidestepping the `__scrml_error` gate (boundary codegen UNCHANGED). SPEC §19.15 + §19.2 amend + §4.15/§24.4 register + §34 ×3. Build: 2 agent crashes (env) → PA-direct finish (user-authorized); both loci (match-arm payload + `@cell`) + reactivity + fence PA-R26-verified; full suite 24,321/0; +6 integration tests. Authority: `scrml-support/docs/deep-dives/error-handling-holistic-2026-06-15.md` + `…/docs/debates/error-handling-display-gap-2026-06-15.md` + design-insight (RATIFIED a/c).
<!-- @gap id=g-held-error-display sev=MED status=resolved -->

### G-RENDER-NOT-ENUM-ASIS-MISS — `<render of=X/>` does not fence a non-enum `of=` target when X's type resolves to `asIs` — `NEW S196; LOW; open`
The §19.15.3 exhaustiveness/type fence fires E-RENDER-NOT-ENUM only when X's `of=` value resolves to a CONCRETE non-enum type. A bare `<name> = "bob"` cell resolves to `asIs` (not concrete `string`), so `<render of=@name/>` does NOT fence — it conservatively emits an inert empty-switch no-op (renders nothing) rather than risk a false positive. Not wrong-output, not a crash; a held NON-enum at a `<render>` site is rare (the canonical use is a held error/Phase enum). Tightening would require concretizing more cell-init types in the typer's `of=` resolution. Surfaced by the S196 PA-direct R26 (the no-false-fire conservatism is the deliberate design choice §19.15.3).
<!-- @gap id=g-render-not-enum-asis-miss sev=LOW status=resolved -->  <!-- RESOLVED S209 (sPA ss3 item4, 631ea548): <render of=@strCell/> now fences E-RENDER-NOT-ENUM vs an inert empty-switch; call/variant/absence/ambiguous stay silent; +9 tests -->

### G-SHORTHAND-INTERP-MATCH-ARM-CODEGEN — `${...}` interpolation inside a `<match>`-arm `:`-shorthand display-text literal (§4.18.4) emits LITERALLY → silent wrong output — `NEW S195; MED; open`
`<Failed reason : "Failed: ${reason}">` COMPILES CLEAN but emits `return "Failed: ${reason}"` literally (the bare-body form `<Failed reason><p>${reason}</p></>` lowers correctly). §4.18.4 normatively specifies `${...}` interpolation inside a `"..."` display-text literal, but it is NOT lowered for the match-arm `:`-shorthand locus — worse than an error: silent wrong output. Surfaced by the error-handling deep-dive (Seam 3 / H2). **RESOLVED S196 (render-expr-prereq-bugs Bucket 4, MATCH-ARM locus only):** emit-match.ts:buildMatchArms recognises a §4.18.3 display-text literal in the shorthand body (`displayTextLiteralInner` decodes the three §4.18.3 escapes), strips the `"..."` delimiters, and routes the INNER content through the SAME free-text fragment lowering the bare-body form uses — segments + `${...}` wire byte-equivalent to `<Variant ...><p>${...}</p></>`. Pre-fix parseExprToNode parsed it as a plain JS string literal. +8 tests. **INVESTIGATE RESULT:** the gap GENERALIZES to the other code-default-body `:`-shorthand loci but in DIFFERENT forms (separate wiring per locus, NOT a single shared-helper drop-in) → filed as g-shorthand-interp-engine-element-loci.
<!-- @gap id=g-shorthand-interp-match-arm-codegen sev=MED status=resolved -->

### G-MATCH-ARM-APOSTROPHE-BS — an apostrophe in `<match>`-arm FREE-TEXT prose breaks the block-splitter — `NEW S195; MED; open`
`<Failed> <p>We'll try again later.</p> </>` → `E-CTX-001` "Unclosed `<match>`" because the block-splitter scanner reads the apostrophe as a string delimiter (control `We will` compiles clean). Failure UI prose routinely uses contractions (Couldn't / We'll / Didn't); the 09 rewrites work around it by banning contractions in arm prose. Same family as the S144 `//`-in-string disambiguation cluster + the S195 `g-blocksplitter-comment-span-not-opaque` (the BS doesn't treat comment/quote spans as opaque in markup-ish free-text). Site: `block-splitter.js` (string-delimiter scan). Surfaced by the 09-(a) + the error-handling deep-dive (Bug 2 / H5). **RESOLVED S196 (render-expr-prereq-bugs Bucket 2):** TWO sites both treated a markup-text-level `'`/`"` as a string-span delimiter — block-splitter.js `findStructuralBodyEnd` (removed the text-level quote-skip + the now-dead `skipQuotedString`) AND match-statechild-parser.ts `findArmCloser` + `findNextArmOpener` OUTER scans. Per the S109 locus ruling, markup-text body is TEXT with no string concept; opener-internal attribute-value / display-text-literal quotes stay tracked (inner opener scan). +8 tests (direct parseMatchArms API + full-pipeline + unclosed-arm negative).
<!-- @gap id=g-match-arm-apostrophe-bs sev=MED status=resolved -->

### G-SHORTHAND-INTERP-ENGINE-ELEMENT-LOCI — `${...}` interpolation inside a `:`-shorthand display-text literal at the ENGINE state-child (§51.0) and §4.14 ELEMENT loci is mishandled — `NEW S196; MED; open`
The S196 Bucket-4 INVESTIGATE pass (sibling of g-shorthand-interp-match-arm-codegen, now RESOLVED for the match-arm locus) confirmed the same display-text-literal-interpolation gap is present at the OTHER two code-default-body `:`-shorthand loci, but in DIFFERENT broken forms — so each needs SEPARATE wiring, NOT the match-arm fix's shared helper: (1) ENGINE state-child §51.0.I — `<Loading pct : "Loading ${pct}%">` drops the WHOLE body (the variant's body render is empty, `"Loading": []`); (2) §4.14 ELEMENT — `<span : "Hello ${@label}!">` lowers ONLY the interpolation (`el.textContent = _scrml_reactive_get("label")`) and DROPS the literal segments (`Hello ` / `!`). The match-arm locus (emit-match.ts) consumed `displayTextLiteralInner` + the free-text fragment route; the engine locus (emit-engine.ts body-render) and the element locus (emit-html.ts `:`-shorthand) have distinct codegen paths that each need the same recognise-literal → route-inner-as-free-text treatment. NOTE a secondary §4.18.6 concern shared by all three (incl. the now-resolved match-arm fix + the bare-body reference): a literal `<`/`>`/`&` in a display-text-literal SEGMENT is currently parsed as markup (via the free-text fragment route) rather than auto-HTML-escaped per §4.18.6 — the canonical errors-as-states case (`"Failed: ${reason}"`, plain text + interp) is byte-correct; the `<`/`&`-in-segment edge matches the bare-body reference but diverges from §4.18.6 strict auto-escape. Surfaced by the S196 render-expr-prereq-bugs Bucket-4 INVESTIGATE. **RESOLVED S209 (sPA ss2 item4, `a4eeaf34`):** the ENGINE locus (§51.0.I) now derives the state-child body from `sc.bodyRaw` when `sc.isColonShorthand` — mirrors the S196 match-arm fix (display-text-literal → `displayTextLiteralInner`→`nativeParseFile`; markup; bare-expr; `displayTextLiteralInner` exported from `emit-match.ts`). The §4.14 ELEMENT locus was verified ALREADY-CORRECT (no change needed). +12 tests. **Residual (minor):** the §4.18.6 secondary auto-escape edge (a literal `<`/`>`/`&` in a display-text SEGMENT parsed as markup rather than auto-escaped) is unaddressed — a documented minor edge, not a render-drop.
<!-- @gap id=g-shorthand-interp-engine-element-loci sev=MED status=resolved -->

### G-SPEC-51-0-S-WORKED-EXAMPLE-NON-EXHAUSTIVE — the §51.0.S engine-message-dispatch worked examples violate their own §51.0.S.2.4 exhaustiveness rule — `NEW S196; LOW; RESOLVED S196`
The §51.0.S.6 end-to-end worked example AND the §51.0.S.2.3 arm-form example both declare `<engine for=DragPhase accepts=DragMsg>` with `<Idle>` covering only `.Start` and `<Dragging>` covering only `.Drop`/`.End` — neither carries a `| _ :>` wildcard over the full DragMsg set `{Start, Drop, End}`. Per §51.0.S.2.4 a state that declares ANY message-arm MUST cover every variant OR carry `| _ :>`, so both examples as written would fire `E-ENGINE-MSG-ARM-NOT-EXHAUSTIVE` (§34) — the section's own worked examples don't compile against the section's own normative rule. CONFIRMED by the S196 corpus-wave-2 verification workflow (the 25-triage-board rewrite mirrors §51.0.S.6; the dev hit the same non-exhaustiveness and added the wildcards to compile). **RESOLVED S196 (PA-direct, SPEC-editorial):** added `| _ :> @dragPhase` (the §51.0.S.2.4-sanctioned self-target stay-in-state no-op, §51.0.F.1) to the `<Idle>` and `<Dragging>` states of both examples. SPEC-text-only; no compiler behavior change. Surfaced by the wave-2 25-triage-board rewrite + the verification workflow.
<!-- @gap id=g-spec-51-0-s-worked-example-non-exhaustive sev=LOW status=resolved -->

## §S210 — gaps filed S210 (2026-06-20, adopter inbox triage: 6nz p10 + flogence dogfood)

> All three verified empirically on HEAD `41422726` per the S138 reverse-direction doctrine (reproduce on real source + cross-check the reporter's described reproducer + check for a sibling-fix window before claiming-open). All three are the compile-clean-but-runtime-broken / silent-miscompile class. Reproducers: 6nz sidecars in `handOffs/incoming/2026-06-20-1217-6nz-p10-bug-sidecars/` (moved to `read/` at re-integration); flogence inline + isolated repro `/tmp` (also in the flogence inbox message).

### g-attr-interp-fn-name-not-renamed — a user-function name is NOT rewritten inside an attribute-value template literal → runtime ReferenceError — `NEW S210; HIGH; open`
A user `function` called inside an HTML **attribute-value** interpolation (`<div class="box box-${tag()}">`) emits the BARE name `tag()` instead of the encoded `_scrml_tag_N()` → `ReferenceError: tag is not defined` at first render. Compile-clean (exit-0, `node --check` OK), silently runtime-broken. The §47 name-encoding rewrite reaches textContent interp + bare calls + `@cell` refs but NOT attribute-value template literals. **Empirically confirmed on HEAD `41422726`** (6nz sidecar `bug-ad-attr-interp-fn-rename.scrml`): emitted `client.js:16` = `setAttribute("class", \`box box-${tag()}\`)` (BARE), while `:24` correctly emits `\`c-${_scrml_reactive_get("n")}\`` for `@n` and `:37` correctly emits `_scrml_render_value(el, _scrml_tag_4())` for the textContent interp — same file, same fn, only the attr-template-literal path misses the rewrite. Common shape `class="card card-${variantOf(x)}"`; killed 6nz p10 on first render. Adjacent to Bug Z (rename-pass interpolation coverage — string-literal half fixed S144 `88071273`; the attr-interp fn-name half is still open). **Likely locus:** the name-encoding/rewrite pass over attribute-value template-literal interpolations (the `@cell` path already rewrites there, so the gap is fn-name-specific). Reporter: 6nz S12 (p10 rebuild). **RESOLVED S210** (agent `ad6ae550`, PA file-delta) — root was NOT the brief's guessed loci (emit-html/emit-event-wiring): the whole-buffer fn-name mangle skipped backtick template-literal `${...}` interpolations because the shared `code-segments.ts rewriteCodeSegments` fence treated template literals as fully opaque. Fixed by descending into `${...}` interp code (static text + plain-quote strings stay opaque, preserving the S144 Bug Z fence) — a general fix (also corrects `not`/`is`-lowering inside `${...}` for all callers). PA-independent R26: `box-${tag()}`→`box-${_scrml_tag_4()}`, @cell/textContent unchanged, node --check clean. Also unlocked a pre-existing test that was LOCKING the miscompile (S96 locked-test pattern; coupled in the same commit). <!-- @gap id=g-attr-interp-fn-name-not-renamed sev=HIGH status=resolved -->

### g-engine-name-attr-swallows-var-duplicate — `name=` on `<engine>` is silently consumed (not a valid engine attr) → bypasses E-ENGINE-VAR-DUPLICATE → runtime-broken write-guard — `NEW S210; HIGH; open`
`<engine name=ModeMachine for=Mode initial=.Nav>` + a separately-declared `@mode` cell compiles exit-0 then throws `E-ENGINE-001-RT: Illegal transition` on EVERY legal transition at runtime. **Root (PA SPEC-cross-check + control test, NOT the reporter's hypothesis):** `name=` is NOT a valid `<engine>` attribute — the §51.0.B attribute set is `for=` / `initial=` / `var=` / `derived=` (`name=` belongs to nested `<program>`, `<onTimeout>`, workers). The compiler **silently consumes** `name=ModeMachine` as a pseudo-var-source (auto-derives the engine cell `modeMachine`) and accepts `@mode: ModeMachine` typed against the engine-name-as-if-a-type, producing two mismatched transition tables (`__scrml_engine_modeMachine_transitions` is built; the `@mode` write-guard looks up a different `__scrml_transitions_ModeMachine`) and NO collision diagnostic. The reporter framed the root as "the write-guard uses the wrong table" — that is a SYMPTOM (dont-soft-classify). **Empirically pinned on HEAD `41422726`:** the canonical `var=mode` + a separate `@mode` cell correctly fires `E-ENGINE-VAR-DUPLICATE` (exit-1); the invalid `name=` form silently bypasses that exact gate (exit-0, runtime-broken). **Fix fork (surface to user):** (a) REJECT `name=` on `<engine>` with a "did you mean `var=`?" hint (canonical-form steer; smallest; matches "`name=` isn't an engine attribute"), OR (b) treat `name=` as a `var=` alias (then E-ENGINE-VAR-DUPLICATE fires correctly via the existing gate). Either closes the silent-runtime-break; (a) is the PA lean (no new alias surface; Pillar-5 keyword discipline). Workaround: canonical no-name `<engine for=Mode initial=.Nav>` (engine owns the var). Reporter: 6nz S12 (p10), sidecar `bug-ae-engine-name-guard.scrml`. **⚠ ROOT-FRAMING ABOVE WAS WRONG (corrected at resolution).** `name=` IS a ratified-canonical `<engine>` attribute (the engineName; §51 P1 / DD1 2026-04-30, "Both `<engine name=N for=T>` and `<machine name=N for=T>` produce identical AST"; ~12 §51 examples; the §7495 machine-typed-cell `@x: N` form). The first fix dispatch (option a, reject) was DISCARDED as a P1 reversal; the §51.0.B table simply omitted `name=` (a doc-gap, now fixed). **RESOLVED S210** (agent a1ad1907, faa213c5, PA file-delta + R26): option (b) — a MODERN `<engine name=N>` registers EMPTY `machine.rules` (its rules live in `engineMeta.stateChildren` → the populated `__scrml_engine_<var>_transitions`), while the §51.3 write-guard pointed at the empty `__scrml_transitions_<Name>` + a phantom `<Name>`→`modeMachine` var (ast-builder var-derivation contradicting §51.0.C). Fix: `symbol-table.ts registerEngineDecl` binds the modern engine to the user's machine-typed cell `@x: N` (§51.3.3, unify not E-ENGINE-VAR-DUPLICATE) + `emit-reactive-wiring.ts` skips the dead empty §51.3 table for modern engines so the populated §51.0 write-guard owns the cell. PA-independent R26: emitted JS now keys write-guard + table + governed var all on `@mode` (`__scrml_engine_mode_transitions`); transition succeeds (no E-ENGINE-001-RT). +§51.0.B name= row. Genuine collision (`var=mode` + separate non-machine-typed `@mode`) STILL fires E-ENGINE-VAR-DUPLICATE. Full suite 24659/0; 88 engine tests pass unchanged (no P1 reversal). <!-- @gap id=g-engine-name-attr-swallows-var-duplicate sev=HIGH status=resolved -->

### g-literal-arg-expr-serializer-wrong-span — a regex/string LITERAL in call-argument position re-serializes the wrong source span → silent miscompile — `NEW S210; HIGH; open`
A regex literal in method-call-arg position (`s.split(/[^a-z0-9]+/)`) emits the `.split()` argument as a space-tokenized re-serialization of the WHOLE enclosing expression instead of just the regex. Secondary: a string literal in call-arg position at a reactive call site (`splitLiteral("a-b-c")`) loses its quotes → `a - b - c`. Both point at the expression serializer's literal-node fallback grabbing the wrong span. **Empirically confirmed on HEAD `41422726`** (isolated repro — regex passed via a cell to avoid the string-quote-loss): emitted `_scrml_splitLiteral_2` body = `return s.split(s . split ( /[^a-z0-9]+/ ) . map ( t => ( { tok : t } ) )).map(...)` — the `.split()` arg is the re-serialized whole expr (silent; compiles GREEN). **Path-sensitive (S138 reverse-direction note):** flogence's minimal repro compiles GREEN + silently-broken; a variant putting the string literal AT the call site instead surfaces LOUDLY as `E-SCOPE-001` (`a`/`b`/`c` undeclared, from `"a-b-c"`→`a - b - c`) — same root, loud-or-silent by path. Common shapes `str.split(/re/)` / `str.replace(/re/,…)` / `str.match(/re/g)`; killed a flogence TF-IDF router (every cosine score → 0). Workaround: bind the regex/string to a `const` and pass by name (an *identifier* in arg position serializes fine). **Likely locus:** the expression/codegen stage lowering method-call arguments where a regex/string-literal AST node has no structured emitter and the fallback computes the wrong source span. Worth a value-asserting regression test (not just "it compiled"). Reporter: flogence PA (dogfood). **RESOLVED S210** (agent `2f94b140`, PA file-delta) — TWO distinct roots (the report's "one root" was wrong; found via minimal repros per cookbook-vs-empirical): Root A regex-literal (`expression-parser.ts` dedicated regex-`Literal` branch carrying `node.raw`; BigInt fallback prefers `raw`) + Root B string-in-braced-body (`ast-builder.js collectBracedBody` now re-quotes STRING tokens, mirroring collectExpr/collectLiftExpr). The original flogence repro used an ident (`@raw`) at its call site so never surfaced Root B. PA-independent R26: `s.split(/[^a-z0-9]+/).map(...)` (arg = just the regex) + the original `splitLiteral("a-b-c")` repro now compiles GREEN with quotes preserved (was loud E-SCOPE-001), node --check clean; value-asserting regression tests added for both roots. <!-- @gap id=g-literal-arg-expr-serializer-wrong-span sev=HIGH status=resolved -->

### g-paren-binary-group-dropped-before-method — a parenthesized binary expr loses its grouping before a member/method access → silent miscompile — `NEW S210; HIGH; RESOLVED S210 (sPA ss3, aae34c26)`
`(a + b).method()` emits as `a + b.method()` — the grouping parens around the binary expr are DROPPED, so the member/method binds to the last operand instead of the whole parenthesized expression; precedence changes → wrong runtime value, GREEN compile, `node --check` clean. **Empirically confirmed on HEAD (post-ss3 `2eea9d4e`)** (flogence minimal repro): `function f(a,b){ return ({ x: (a + " " + b).toUpperCase() }) }` emits `return {x: a + " " + b.toUpperCase()};` — parens gone, `.toUpperCase()` binds to `b` alone. Killed a flogence TF-IDF router (a parenthesized `(r.project + " " + r.text).toLowerCase().split(...)` re-associated → garbage → every cosine score collapsed to ~0). **Same FAMILY as the resolved `g-literal-arg-expr-serializer-wrong-span` (above) + the sibling `g-isop-call-tail-lhs-paren-miscompile` (below)** — the expression serializer mishandles parenthesization (grouping-paren-vs-call/operand span). Workaround: bind the parenthesized expr to a `const` first, then call the method on the identifier (an identifier in receiver position serializes fine). **Likely locus:** the expression serializer drops grouping parens when a parenthesized binary expr is the receiver of a member access — re-serializes `a + b` without re-wrapping. Reporter: flogence PA (dogfood, TF-IDF tokenizer). Worth a value-asserting regression test (emitted text for `(a+b).m()` parens preserved). **RESOLVED S210 (sPA ss3 item1, `aae34c26`):** a `receiverNeedsParens` guard at `emitMember`/`emitIndex`/`emitCall`/`emitNew` (`emit-expr.ts`) — the receiver-position sibling of Bug W / S205 — + closed the identical gap in `emitStringFromTree` (`expression-parser.ts`, defense-in-depth). R26 value-asserted (emit-string + e2e); +1 integration test + receiver cases. **board HIGH 1→0.** <!-- @gap id=g-paren-binary-group-dropped-before-method sev=HIGH status=resolved -->

### g-isop-call-tail-lhs-paren-miscompile — is-op with a call-tail LHS silently miscompiles in `--mode library` — `NEW S210; MED; RESOLVED S210 (sPA ss3, d004e6b9)`
In `--mode library` line-rewrite, an is-op whose LHS ends in a call (`re.exec(s) is some`) emits `re.exec((s) != null)` — `_rewriteParenthesizedIsOp` grabs the CALL's own argument parens instead of treating the whole call as the LHS. Valid JS so NO `E-CODEGEN-INVALID-JS` (silent-WRONG — arguably higher impact than the LOUD `bug-18` computed-LHS case it sat beside). Separate root from bug-18 (the paren-rewrite has no grouping-paren-vs-call guard); **same FAMILY as `g-paren-binary-group-dropped-before-method` (above) + the resolved `g-literal-arg-expr-serializer-wrong-span`** — a future "expression-serializer paren/span" sPA cluster. Repro: `export function f(re,s){ return re.exec(s) is some ? "h" : "n" }` `--mode library`. sPA-ss3 residual (surfaced finishing item2, out of bug-18's surgical scope). Locus: `codegen/rewrite.ts _rewriteParenthesizedIsOp`. **RESOLVED S210 (sPA ss3 item2, `d004e6b9`):** `_rewriteParenthesizedIsOp` now distinguishes a grouping paren from a call paren (keyword-aware) + captures the whole call chain single-eval via `_scanChainStartLeft`. R26: +14 runtime assertions + node --check; +9 `not-keyword.test.js` tests. <!-- @gap id=g-isop-call-tail-lhs-paren-miscompile sev=MED status=resolved -->

### g-input-state-markup-nonreactive-lint — `W-INPUT-STATE-MARKUP-NONREACTIVE` lint planned (§36.6) but not yet fired — `NEW S210; LOW; open (ruling = by-design; lint impl pending)`
6nz AF: `${<#id>.x}` (an input-state read in a markup interpolation) compiles render-once with NO diagnostic — a silent footgun (an editor wanting live cursor coords in its chrome gets a one-shot value). **RULING S210 (user "confirm AF"): the non-reactivity is BY-DESIGN** — §36.6 is normative ("Input state is read at the moment of the `animationFrame` callback — no reactive subscriptions are set up. This is intentional"); input-state is a live-read source, NOT a reactive cell; the `@cell`-bridge (read `<#id>` in an `animationFrame` loop → assign `@cell` → interpolate the cell) is the reactive pattern. NOT a codegen gap. **Done this turn (PA-direct, SPEC currency):** §36.1 clarified (dropped the "reactive access / same lifecycle as `<poll>`" overclaim — `<poll>` IS subscribable, input-state is not) + §36.6 markup-interp note added. **IMPL pending (this gap):** the planned info-lint `W-INPUT-STATE-MARKUP-NONREACTIVE` — fire when an input-state `<#id>` read appears inside a markup interpolation (NOT inside an `animationFrame`/logic body); point at the @cell-bridge. Locus: the markup-interp pass where `@cell` interps get the `_scrml_effect` wrapper (detect the `<#id>`-read-without-wrapper case). §34 row lands WITH the impl (Rule 4). Reporter: 6nz AF (p10). <!-- @gap id=g-input-state-markup-nonreactive-lint sev=LOW status=open -->

### g-block-match-in-lift-misparsed-as-components — block `<match>` inside `${ for … lift }` mis-parses its arms as components → misleading E-COMPONENT-035 — `NEW S210; LOW; RESOLVED S213`
A per-item block `<match for=T on=expr>` placed inside a `${ for (…) { lift <li>…</li> } }` Tier-0 loop fails: the variant arm tags (`<Open>`/`<Closed>`) are not recognized as match arms in the lift context, fall through to the uppercase-tag→component path, and are rejected with `E-COMPONENT-035` + `E-COMPONENT-020` whose hint blames "cross-file component import is not yet supported" — sending the adopter after a phantom component-import problem. The SAME block `<match>` inside the Tier-1 `<each>` tag works (renders correctly). **Empirically confirmed on HEAD `41422726`** (giti S11 happy-dom sweep + PA re-compile): the `${for…lift}` form fails `E-COMPONENT-035` ×2; the `<each>` form compiles. Not a silent miscompile (fails loudly) — the gap is ERROR QUALITY + a parse-context gap (block-match arm recognition doesn't extend into the Tier-0 lift loop body). **Fix shape (TBD):** either support block-`<match>` inside `${ … lift }`, OR emit a targeted diagnostic ("block `<match>` is not supported inside a `${ … lift }` loop; use `<each>`"). Workaround: use the `<each>` form. giti's UI renders lists almost entirely via `${for…lift}`, so a per-row `<match>` is a natural reach. Reporter: giti S11 (client-tier dogfood). **sPA ss4 (S212) — ROOT PINNED + PARKED (user ruling).** Re-confirmed on HEAD; root = the `lift`-body re-parse `liftBareDeclarations` does NOT route `<match>` through the S107 match-block recognition that the `<each>` body path uses (which is why the same block `<match>` in `<each>` compiles). The fix-shape fork is a **language-capability ruling → PA/dPA**: (a) support block-`<match>` in `${…lift}` (parity with `<each>`; cohesive, touches the lift parse-context) vs (b) targeted diagnostic only ("use `<each>`"; lowest effort, aligns with the S130 HU-1 `<each>`-is-canonical direction). The sPA escalated rather than decide; the user ruled PARK pending the (a)/(b) ruling. **RULED S212 — (b) targeted diagnostic, steer to `<each>` (user verbatim "(b) targeted diagnostic, steer to <each>").** Rationale: aligns with the S130 HU-1 `<each>`-is-canonical direction + limit-the-primitives (don't widen the legacy `${for…lift}` parse-context to support a form the language is steering away from). **READY (not fired) — LOW dispatch:** in the `lift`-body re-parse path (`liftBareDeclarations` / block-splitter lift-context), detect a block-`<match>` opener (uppercase variant arms following a `<match for= on=>`) and emit a NEW targeted §34 Error (e.g. `E-MATCH-BLOCK-IN-LIFT`) — "block `<match>` is not supported inside a `${ … lift }` loop; use the `<each>` form" — REPLACING the misleading `E-COMPONENT-035`/`-020` cascade (suppress those for this shape). §34 row lands WITH the impl (Rule 4). Option (a) support-the-form REJECTED. Reporter: giti S11; ruling user S212. **RESOLVED S213 (PA-direct).** Detect-at-VP-2: `compiler/src/validators/post-ce-invariant.ts` `collectUnrecognizedMatchBlocks` pre-scans for a residual `kind:"markup" tag:"match"` node carrying a `for=` attr — the recognized block-form is `kind:"match-block"` (built by the BS S107 path / `<each>`-body + markup-position), so ONLY the lift/logic-context inline-markup path leaves a raw match-markup node, which IS the unrecognized-block-match signal. It emits ONE `E-MATCH-BLOCK-IN-LIFT` (names the `for=` type + steers to `<each>`) and collects the `<match>`'s uppercase-tag arm descendants into a suppression set so the E-COMPONENT-035 walk skips them — the misleading cascade is REPLACED, not supplemented. NEW §34 row `E-MATCH-BLOCK-IN-LIFT` (§18.0.1 / §17.7). Option (a) support-the-form REJECTED per the ruling (limit-primitives; `<each>` canonical per S130 HU-1). PA-independent R26 (reverse-direction reproduced on HEAD `ca712295` first): the `${for…lift}` repro → 1× `E-MATCH-BLOCK-IN-LIFT`, 0× `E-COMPONENT-035`; the `<each>` form still GREEN. +3 unit tests (`compiler/tests/unit/uvb-w1-post-ce-invariant.test.js` §7; file 9→12 pass). <!-- @gap id=g-block-match-in-lift-misparsed-as-components sev=LOW status=resolved -->
