<!-- @gap id=g-validator-inline-msg-colon-form sev=MED status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S185 dog-food (§55 validators / auto-synth validity surface). DOC migration DONE S185 (paren-canonical, user-ruled); compiler diagnostic fix OPEN.**

**Symptom.** A cell declared with the **colon-form** inline-message override — `<name req:"…msg…">` — silently CORRUPTS the cell's `@`-access registration. Every subsequent `@cell` / `@parent.field` reference fires a MISLEADING `E-SCOPE-001` ("Unquoted identifier `@cell` cannot be resolved … did you mean `@@cell`?"), pointing at the *cell* rather than at the malformed validator. The field render-by-tag (`<name/>`) still resolves; only the `@`-prefixed canonical-access path breaks. NOT compound-specific — reproduces on a top-level cell (`<ref req:"required"> = <input/>` + `@ref`) AND a compound child (breaks the compound PARENT `@signup`). Confirmed HEAD `a250348a`.

**Root + canonical form (Rule 4).** The §55.10-NORMATIVE Level-1 inline override is the **paren** form — a trailing string-literal ARG inside the validator parens: `<name req("Please enter your name") length(>=2, "…")>` (SPEC §55.10 body :30971 + §34 `E-VALIDATOR-INLINE-DYNAMIC` :16931, both paren). The `validator-arg-parser.ts` (`:87`/`:126`) is built entirely around the paren-arg shape; the paren form COMPILES CLEAN + `@`-access resolves (verified). The colon form `req:"…"` is NOT valid scrml — the `:` collides with the decl scanner's colon handling (type-annotation / §4.14 `:`-shorthand), corrupting the state-decl registration. The colon form only ever appeared in 2 STRAY doc-summary sites that drifted from the normative §55.10 (PRIMER §8 + SPEC §41.12) — NOT in the normative definition, and ZERO corpus uses (`grep 'req:"' tests/samples/examples` = 0). No test exercises the source `req("…")` / `req:"…"` forms end-to-end (the c10 tests cover the runtime `messageFor` path with synthesized inputs).

**User ruling S185:** paren-canonical; migrate the docs; file MED.

**DONE S185 (doc migration):** PRIMER §8:797 + SPEC §41.12:20616 colon-form → paren form (`req("…")`), each with a "the colon form `req:"…"` is NOT valid scrml" note. SPEC §55.10 + §34 were already paren (normative-correct). Kickstarter + corpus already clean.

**RESOLVED S185 (compiler diagnostic fix).** `ast-builder.js scanStructuralDeclLookahead` now detects the colon-form inline-message override — a KNOWN universal-core predicate (per `validator-catalog.ts`) immediately followed by `:` STRING INSIDE the opener (before `>`), in both the bareword (`req:"…"`) and call-form (`length(>=2):"…"`) shapes — via the new `tryRecoverColonInlineMessage` helper. It fires the new Error `E-VALIDATOR-INLINE-COLON` (§34 + §55 summary; cross-ref §55.10/§41.12) naming the paren form `req("…")` as the resolution, AND RECOVERS by attaching the message as the paren-form inline-override arg (JSON-stringified trailing string slot) — so the cell registers WITH the inline override and the misleading `E-SCOPE-001` cascade does NOT fire. The legit typed-cell `<name>: T` decl (the `:` lives AFTER the `>`, handled by the `typedDecl` branch) and the canonical paren form are untouched. Verified R26 (repro-1 top-level + repro-2 compound → 1×COLON / 0×SCOPE; control-a paren + control-b typed-cell → 0/0) + the original dog-food reproducers (primer-verbatim/bisect-h/dispatch-form → 1×COLON / 0×SCOPE each). +coupled unit test `compiler/tests/unit/validator-inline-colon.test.js` (10 tests). Reproducers at `docs/changes/validator-inline-colon-diagnostic-2026-06-12/repro/`.

**Fix prescription (LANDED S185 — see RESOLVED note above; retained for the record):** the colon form emits a CLEAR diagnostic (`E-VALIDATOR-INLINE-COLON` → "inline message override uses the paren form `req(\"…\")`, not `req:\"…\"`") instead of silently corrupting cell registration + emitting the misleading `E-SCOPE-001` about the cell being undeclared. Per don't-soft-classify: a malformed validator that mis-reports an unrelated identifier as undeclared is a diagnostic bug. Fire site: the structural-decl / validator scanner (`ast-builder.js scanStructuralDeclLookahead` `tryRecoverColonInlineMessage`); the `@`-access `E-SCOPE-001` cascade is suppressed by the cell-registration recovery. Reproducers: `docs/changes/validator-inline-colon-diagnostic-2026-06-12/repro/`.

<!-- @gap id=g-derived-engine-expression-form sev=LOW status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S185 dog-food (engine §51 centerpiece). Known B16 deferral; doc-vs-impl on the centerpiece + confusing diagnostics.**

**Symptom.** The derived-engine **expression form** `<engine for=T derived=expr>` (§51.0.J Move-14 / L20 / PRIMER §7 — "reactively recomputes the variant; no rules, no writes, no initial=") is NOT implemented. Only the LEGACY form `derived=@machineVar` (B16 `legacy-source-var`, where `@machineVar` is itself a machine-typed reactive) is recognized. An adopter writing the documented expression form gets confusing diagnostics:
- `derived=@miles > 500 ? .High : .Low` → `E-ENGINE-004` ("Derived machine references source variable `@miles`, but no machine-bound reactive with that name was found") — the parser grabs the first `@var` as a legacy source-var.
- `derived=(@miles > 500 ? .High : .Low)` / `derived=${ … }` → falls through to NON-derived treatment → `W-ENGINE-INITIAL-MISSING` ("non-derived engines must specify initial="), and an illegal write to the cell fires `E-ENGINE-INVALID-TRANSITION` instead of the correct `E-DERIVED-ENGINE-NO-WRITE` (§51.0.J).

**Root.** Known B16 deferral — PRIMER §13.7 B16 specifics: "When ast-builder learns the §51.0.J `derived=match @x { … }` form, it'll set `derivedExpr` to a parsed ExprNode … At that point the B16 SYM rejections (E-DERIVED-ENGINE-NO-INITIAL / -NO-RULES / -NO-WRITE) fire automatically." The SYM-side rejections + DG cycle-detection (B16) are wired + gated on `derivedExpr.kind !== "legacy-source-var"`; they're dormant because the ast-builder never produces a non-legacy `derivedExpr`. So the impl is spec-ahead: §51.0.J is normative, B16 wired the consumer side, the ast-builder parse of the expression form is the missing piece.

**Severity LOW (user-ruled S185).** Spec-ahead-of-impl + a real (larger) build (ast-builder expression-form parse → populate `derivedExpr` as a parsed ExprNode → the dormant B16 rejections light up). The CONFUSING-diagnostic facet (W-ENGINE-INITIAL-MISSING / E-ENGINE-004 / E-ENGINE-INVALID-TRANSITION on a `derived=`-bearing opener) is the adopter-visible part; a cheaper interim fix could detect a `derived=` attribute whose value isn't a bare `@machineVar` and emit a clear "derived engine expression form not yet implemented (§51.0.J); use `derived=@machineVar` or a plain engine" diagnostic. **Doc note:** PRIMER §7 presents `derived=expr` as a working feature while §13.7 B16 records it deferred — a doc-vs-impl inconsistency on the centerpiece (consider a PRIMER §7 "expression form spec-ahead" caveat at fix/clarify time). Reproducers staged at `/tmp/dogfood-engine/` (d-bare-expr / d-match-form / derived.scrml / derived-write.scrml).

**RESOLVED S190 (`derived-engine-expression-form-2026-06-13`, agent `a52be30f9cc11223c`, FINAL_SHA `19a557f1`, PA-landed via file-delta; user ruled S190 "full feature build now").** The §51.0.J expression form is implemented end-to-end. **Parser** (`ast-builder.js` + `block-splitter.js`): `derived=` value classified bare-ident (legacy) / `match @x {...}` (inline-match) / `<expr>` (ternary/call/conditional); the BS+ast-builder opener scanner is now operator-aware inside a `derived=<expr>` value (comparison `>`/`<`/`>=`/`<=` = operator not opener-close; ternary `?`-depth keeps the `:` from being a §4.14 `:`-shorthand — OPPOSITE polarity to the S188 cluster-A reject, tightly gated to `derived=` only so non-derived attrs are unaffected); produces a structured `derivedExprNode`. **symbol-table.ts**: three `derivedExpr.kind`s (`legacy-source-var`/`inline-match`/`expr`); the `expr` kind enumerates EVERY `@cell` upstream (multi-cell `@miles + @bonus` subscribes to both); B16 NO-RULES/-NO-INITIAL/-NO-WRITE/-CIRCULAR light up for any non-legacy kind; NO-RULES extended to catch a state-child `rule=` ATTRIBUTE (pre-S190 only the arrow shape was detected). **type-system.ts**: modern forms skip the §51.9 `validateDerivedMachines` projection path (which mis-fired E-ENGINE-004/018) — registered as ordinary MachineTypes so B15/B16 own their diagnostics; the legacy §51.9 path is UNTOUCHED. **codegen** (`emit-engine.ts` + `dependency-graph.ts`): reactive recompute via the C14 `_scrml_derived_*` substrate + per-upstream DG edges. PA-independent R26 (S138 dual-verify): match/ternary/call/multi-cell compile + wire `_scrml_derived_subscribe` to all source cells; all 6 rejection codes fire; state-child `effect=` legal; `node --check` clean; full suite 24100/0. SPEC §51.0.J +non-match worked example (Rule 4); PRIMER §13.7 B16 → landed. Native-parser deferred (~v0.8 cutover; `derivedExprText`/`derivedExprNode` STRIP_KEY'd LIVE-only). +16 tests (`derived-engine-expression-form.test.js`).

### G-LEGACY-DERIVED-PROJECTION-PLAIN-CELL — legacy `derived=@machineVar` projection over a PLAIN enum cell (non-machine source) fires E-ENGINE-004 full-pipeline, but the c14 unit test passes (codegen-direct, skips validateDerivedMachines) — `NEW S190; LOW; pre-existing §51.9 test-vs-pipeline gap`
<!-- @gap id=g-legacy-derived-projection-plain-cell sev=LOW status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S190 (derived-engine-expression-form build, agent `a52be30f9cc11223c` Phase-0 + PA-independent R26).** The LEGACY §51.9 `derived=@machineVar` 1:1 projection requires the source to be a MACHINE-bound reactive (§51.9.3). Over a PLAIN enum cell (`@order: Phase` where `Phase` is a `:enum`, NOT a `:machine`), `<engine for=Health derived=@order>` fires **`E-ENGINE-004`** through the full compile pipeline. **The catch:** `compiler/tests/unit/c14-derived-engines.test.js` exercises exactly this shape (`derived=@order` over a plain `Phase` cell) and PASSES — because it drives `runUpToSYM` + `generateClientJs(makeTestCtx(...))` DIRECTLY, skipping the type-system `validateDerivedMachines` pass that fires E-ENGINE-004 in the real `compile()`. So the codegen substrate is correct but unreachable full-pipeline for the plain-cell source. **PRE-EXISTING** (verified at the pre-S190 baseline; the derived-engine-expression-form build changed NOTHING in the §51.9 legacy path — its type-system change only adds an early-SKIP for the MODERN `inlineMatchBody`/`derivedExprNode` forms). **The genuinely-working full-pipeline legacy form is `examples/14-mario`** where the source is itself an engine auto-cell (machine-bound). **Severity LOW** — narrow (plain-cell legacy projection; the modern §51.0.J `derived=match @x {...}` form now covers arbitrary mapping from any cell, landed S190; and `const <x> = match @y {...}` derived cells cover the non-engine case). **The real question (separate §51.9-vs-§51.0.J boundary):** should the legacy `derived=@machineVar` projection accept a plain enum cell, or is machine-bound-source the intended §51.9.3 constraint (with the c14 test being the bug — it should drive `compile()` not the codegen shortcut)? **Fix direction options:** (a) tighten the c14 test to full-pipeline + accept E-ENGINE-004 as correct (machine-source is required); (b) relax §51.9.3 to accept plain enum cells full-pipeline; (c) deprecate the legacy plain-cell projection in favor of the new modern `derived=match` form. Needs a user ruling. Repro: a `<engine for=Health derived=@order>` with `@order: SomeEnum` (plain enum, not machine).

**RULED S190 (decision pass): "Test-truth + clearer error" (option a).** Keep §51.9.3 (machine-bound source REQUIRED) — NO language widening. Fix: (1) fix `c14-derived-engines.test.js` to drive the FULL `compile()` pipeline (not the `generateClientJs(makeTestCtx(...))` codegen-direct shortcut) so the test reflects reality — a plain-cell `derived=@var` source correctly fires E-ENGINE-004 / OR migrate the test's source to a machine-bound cell (or the modern `derived=match` form); (2) improve the E-ENGINE-004 message so a plain-cell `derived=@var` legacy-projection source STEERS the author to the modern `derived=match @var {...}` form (verified S190: it works over a plain enum cell — `_scrml_derived_subscribe("health","order")`), which supersedes the plain-cell legacy case. Decisive corpus fact: plain-cell legacy projection is CORPUS-DEAD (the one real `derived=` usage is machine-bound `examples/14-mario`, which works); the modern form covers the plain-cell case. Per limit-primitives — don't widen a legacy form the modern form replaces; make the test honest + the diagnostic helpful. Execution: small (test + diagnostic message); queue for dispatch/PA-direct.

**RESOLVED S190 (`legacy-derived-projection-plain-cell-2026-06-13`, agent `a065d7df0cdc9af0c`, FINAL_SHA `7fb9108d`, PA-landed via file-delta).** Both halves landed; §51.9.3 machine-source requirement KEPT (no language widening). **Fix 1 (message):** `type-system.ts validateDerivedMachines` E-ENGINE-004 message now names the legacy §51.9.3 machine-source requirement AND steers a plain enum/struct cell source to the modern §51.0.J `derived=match @var { .SourceVariant => .TargetVariant, ... }` form (PA-independent R26: plain-cell `derived=@order` fires E-ENGINE-004 with the `derived=match @order` steer present). **Fix 2 (c14 test honesty):** agent chose approach (b) — kept the codegen-direct §C14.8/9/10 substrate unit tests (correct in isolation; they deliberately bypass `validateDerivedMachines`) + added a NEW `§C14.15` full-pipeline boundary block (2 `compileScrml`-driven tests) asserting the plain-cell shape fires E-ENGINE-004 (boundary pinned as intended) + the modern form is the plain-cell path; retired the stale "NOT YET PARSED" docstring + added cross-ref notes. Approach (a) was tried + rejected (machine-bound source trips E-ENGINE-018 — legacy form needs projection RULES not C14 state-children — and would lose the legacy-source-var identity-projection coverage). NO SPEC change (the §51.9.3 rule + §34 E-ENGINE-004 row already exist; impl-message + test only). mario flagship clean (no regression); full gate 16,873/0. +2 tests.

<!-- @gap id=g-lifecycle-struct-field-const-notfire sev=LOW status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S183 dog-food (round 5).** The PRIMER §6.5 verbatim worked example — `type User:struct = { ..., passwordHash: (not to string) }; const u: User = {..., passwordHash: not}; const leak = u.passwordHash` (annotated `// E-TYPE-001 - pre-transition access`) — compiled CLEAN (exit 0), NO `E-TYPE-001`. This is §5-Landing-1's STATED scope ("per-access transition-state tracking for **struct fields**", SHIPPED S130 `1feaedc9` + 25 tests), so it SHOULD fire. **CANDIDATE, not yet a confirmed bug** (verify-before-claim / S138 reverse-direction): Landing-1 shipped + tested, so the most likely cause is a sub-path the tracker doesn't observe (e.g. top-level-`${}` `const u: User = {...}` construction + member-read, vs the form Landing-1's tests exercise) rather than a wholesale regression. **Needs a focused gate-logic check** (does E-TYPE-001 fire on Landing-1's own test form vs the primer's `const`-bound top-level form?) before classifying bug-vs-form. Cross-ref §5 lifecycle table Landing 1 + B-prereq.

PRIMER §6.5 + kickstarter §3.2 taught the feature with a plain local `const u: User = {…}` binding read via bare `u.passwordHash` — a TS idiom that is none of §14.12.3's enumerated positions and that the tracker doesn't observe. Both examples rewritten to the cell-form this session. **Side-find fixed same arc:** a trailing `//`/`/* */` comment on a `(not to string)` lifecycle struct-field line leaked into the type-expr → false `E-STRUCT-FUNCTION-FIELD` (blocked valid scrml; hit the canonical SPEC §14.12.1 / PRIMER / kickstarter examples as printed). Root-caused upstream of the PA hypothesis: `ast-builder.js` `collectBracedBody`/`parseLogicBody` pushed COMMENT-token text into `decl.raw`; fixed by skipping COMMENT tokens at collection (one central guard; +12 tests; 0 regressions). PA-independent R26 verified (0 E-STRUCT-FUNCTION-FIELD on the comment form; E-TYPE-001 fires; real `() -> void` field still rejected — no over-strip). ### G-CHANNEL-RECONNECT-BARE-INT — `<channel reconnect=N>` + `<program channel-reconnect=N>` reject the bare-integer form (E-SCOPE-001) the SPEC worked examples use — `NEW S186; LOW; channel-attr registry gap`
<!-- @gap id=g-channel-reconnect-bare-int sev=LOW status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S186 dog-food (channels §38, dispatch-board probe).** A bare integer `<channel name="chat" reconnect=2000>` — the EXACT form in every SPEC §38.2 / §38.6.2 / §38.10.3 worked example, typed "integer (ms)" at §38.3 — fails with `E-SCOPE-001` ("Unquoted identifier `2000` in attribute `reconnect` cannot be resolved … Did you mean to quote it as a string (`\"2000\"`)"). The project-level `<program channel-reconnect=5000>` (§38.3.1) fails identically. Quoted (`reconnect="2000"`) compiles; absent compiles.

**Root + classification (verify-before-claim).** Bare-numeric attributes ARE accepted generally — `<each of=10>` ✅ and engine `<onTimeout after=2000 to=.X/>` ✅ both compile bare. The rejection is LOCALIZED to the reconnect family: `reconnect` / `channel-reconnect` aren't registered as numeric/value-bearing attributes, so a bare integer falls through to the generic identifier-resolution path (the TS-pass attribute-scope check) → `E-SCOPE-001`. The SPEC's bare form is canonical and consistent with the working sibling attrs → this is a COMPILER bug, not a SPEC-example error. **Fix:** register `reconnect` (on `<channel>`) + `channel-reconnect` (on `<program>`) as numeric value-attributes so a bare integer is accepted (mirror how `<each of=>` / `<onTimeout after=>` are handled). `extractChannelAttrs` (`emit-channel.ts:269-276`) already `parseInt`s either a string-literal OR a `.name`-stripped value, so codegen tolerates both shapes once the TS-pass stops rejecting bare. Repro: `/tmp/df-channels/v-bare.scrml` (fails) vs `v-quoted.scrml` (clean). **Fix dispatched S186** (bundled with g-channel-handler-wiring — `docs/changes/channel-codegen-fixes-2026-06-12/`).

**RESOLVED S186** (`channel-codegen-fixes-2026-06-12`, agent `a06f1df4c51155e5e`, FINAL_SHA `2dda0642`, PA-landed). `type-system.ts visitAttr` now exempts `reconnect` + `channel-reconnect` from the E-SCOPE-001 scope-check (mirrors the `ref` guard) — targeted to the two spec-typed integer-ms attrs only. PA-independent R26: bare `reconnect=2000`/`reconnect=3000` compile clean + thread `setTimeout(_connect, N)`; quoted form still clean; bare `<input value=42>` STILL errors (no over-relax). +5 unit tests (§27). **RESIDUAL (pre-existing, separate gap-worthy if it recurs):** `<program channel-reconnect=N>` project-default does NOT thread into the client `onclose` cadence (emits `2000`, not `N`) — a distinct `extractChannelAttrs`/`emitChannelClientJs` `projectReconnectDefault`-wiring gap, NOT the scope-check fix this gap covered. Agent-surfaced; left unfixed (out of scope).

### G-BARE-LITERAL-ATTR-VALUE — bare-integer `interval=` (`<poll>`/`<timer>`) + sibling SPEC-documented value-attrs reject E-SCOPE-001 — same class as the S186-RESOLVED g-channel-reconnect-bare-int — `NEW S192 dog-food; LOW; per-attribute value-registration incomplete`
<!-- @gap id=g-bare-literal-attr-value sev=LOW status=resolved -->  <!-- RESOLVED S209 (sPA ss3 item3, de9d3a12): value-aware bare-literal exemption in visitAttr for spec-typed structural attrs; @-ref still scope-checks; +8 tests -->

**Surfaced S192 dog-food (while waiting on the registration arc).** Bare numeric/boolean literals in unquoted attribute values are handled INCONSISTENTLY per-attribute: the unquoted-attribute scanner reads an UNregistered attr's bare value as an IDENTIFIER-to-resolve → `E-SCOPE-001` ("Unquoted identifier `5000` in attribute `interval` cannot be resolved … Did you mean to quote it as a string"). SAME ROOT as the S186-RESOLVED **g-channel-reconnect-bare-int** (above): attributes registered as numeric/value-bearing accept bare literals; unregistered ones fall through to identifier-resolution.

**Characterized (against main, S192):**
- ACCEPTS bare literals ✓ (registered value-attrs): `default=0`/`default=false`/`default=not` · `<each of=10>` · engine `<onTimeout after=2000>` · the S186-exempted `reconnect=2000`/`channel-reconnect=5000` · validator args `min(18)` · ternary/expr in `${}`.
- REJECTS bare literals ✗ (E-SCOPE-001, unregistered): **`<poll interval=5000>` / `<timer interval=1000>`** (the clear bug — SPEC §6.7.6 documents the bare form throughout: `<timer interval=1000>`, `<timer interval=1000/>`, the E-LIFECYCLE-009 example `<poll interval=1000>`); HTML numeric `maxlength=5`/`step=0.5`; HTML boolean `disabled=true`; `running=false` (§6.7.6-documented); `if=1`. Negative `tabindex=-1` → E-ATTR-001 (a separate `-`-scanner sub-case).
- The real corpus `samples/compilation-tests/gauntlet-r10-elixir-chat.scrml` fails on bare `interval=5000`/`2000`/`1500`.

**Classification + fix (extends the S186 pattern; NOT a general bare-literal relax).** S186 set the project stance via the reconnect fix: register the SPEC-documented value-attr in `type-system.ts visitAttr` (mirror the `ref` guard), deliberately WITHOUT over-relax ("bare `<input value=42>` STILL errors"). So the ACTIONABLE core here is the same shape: register the SPEC-documented bare numeric attrs the per-attribute approach missed — **`interval=` on `<poll>`/`<timer>` is the clear one** (SPEC-documented bare, exactly the reconnect class). The HTML-passthrough attrs (`maxlength`/`step`/`disabled`) are arguably quote-or-`${}`-required under the no-over-relax stance — but `interval=`/`running=` on the §6.7.6 `<poll>`/`<timer>` structural elements are SPEC-documented bare and should be registered. **Fix:** audit the §6.7.6 `<poll>`/`<timer>` attribute schema + register the integer/boolean value-attrs (`interval`, `running`, …) as value-bearing (S186 `reconnect` precedent); confirm a bare `<input value=42>` still errors (no over-relax).

**Workaround:** quote (`interval="1000"`) or interpolate (`${1000}`). **Cross-ref:** g-channel-reconnect-bare-int (RESOLVED S186 — the sibling instance + the established fix pattern). Direction is impl-side per the S186 precedent; the dog-food's initial "general-accept vs SPEC-quote" framing was superseded once the targeted-exemption stance was found.

---

### G-CHANNEL-HANDLER-WIRING — channel event-handler attributes (`onserver:*` / `onclient:*`) are not wired into the emitted WS handlers from real source — `NEW S186; MED; codegen + route-inference`
<!-- @gap id=g-channel-handler-wiring sev=MED status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S186 dog-food (channels §38). The headline real-time feature is non-functional end-to-end from real source** (channels are a zero-adopter sliver, so impact-in-practice is low — hence MED not HIGH).

**Symptom.** All six channel event-handler attributes — `onserver:open` / `onserver:message` / `onserver:close` (server `_scrml_ws_handlers`) and `onclient:open` / `onclient:close` / `onclient:error` (client IIFE `ws.on*`) — parse correctly but NEVER wire into the emitted WS handlers. Emitted output: `_ws.onopen = () => {}` (empty), `_ws.onclose = () => { _reconn = setTimeout(...) }` (reconnect only), server `message(ws, raw)` handles only the `__sync` wire-format. Worse, the referenced handler functions then get **route-inferred as ordinary HTTP RPC endpoints** (`/_scrml/__ri_route_<fn>`) + client fetch stubs — so the `onclient:*` handlers leak SERVER-side code, violating §38.10 ("`onclient:*` run on the client only … SHALL NOT emit server-side code"). Net: a channel can auto-sync cells (works) but cannot run ANY declared message/lifecycle handler.

**Root (pinned, airtight).** The parser emits these attr values as `kind: "call-ref"` (`{name, args:[…], argExprNodes:[…]}` — the canonical event-handler call-ref shape, same as `onclick=handler(e)` §5.2.2). But `emit-channel.ts`'s `attrToCall` — in BOTH `extractChannelHandlers` (`:294-308`) and `extractClientHandlers` (`:323-337`) — only recognizes `kind: "call" | "variable-ref" | "string-literal"`, NOT `"call-ref"` → returns `null` for every real-source handler → empty emission. The `channel.test.js` unit tests pass because (a) the "attr is present" tests (`:273`) assert only `a.name`, never the value KIND, and (b) the emit tests (`:658` "emits onopen= handler when onclient:open is specified") feed a HAND-SYNTHESIZED `makeCallAttr(name, fn, args)` → `{kind:"call"}` (the stale shape), bypassing the parser. This is the exact S138 R26 canary ("regression tests synthesize AST → pass; real-source compile → fails").

**Fix (3 parts).** (a) `attrToCall` recognize `kind:"call-ref"` (map `name` + `args[]` → `name(args.join(", "))`) in both extractors — wires the handlers into emit-channel's server `message()` (onserver:message → `JSON.parse` → `handler(msg)` per §38.6.1) + client `ws.on{open,close,error}`. (b) route-inference must EXCLUDE channel-handler-referenced functions from RPC route + client-fetch-stub emission (closes the §38.10 server-leak; RI already tracks `onserver:message` handlers for reachability per `reachability/component-3.ts` — extend that recognition to suppress route emission). (c) update the `makeCallAttr` test helper to `call-ref` (or add real-source-parse → emit assertions) to close the canary. **R26 MANDATORY before claim-closed** (S138 doctrine — codegen fix relying on AST construction). Repros: `/tmp/df-channels/m-handlers.scrml` (minimal, spec §38.6.1-shaped) + `dispatch-board.scrml`. **Fix dispatched S186** (`docs/changes/channel-codegen-fixes-2026-06-12/`).

**RESOLVED S186** (`channel-codegen-fixes-2026-06-12`, agent `a06f1df4c51155e5e`, FINAL_SHA `2dda0642`, PA-landed; all 3 parts). **(2a)** `emit-channel.ts channelAttrToCall` recognizes `kind:"call-ref"` (+ `messageParam` §38.6.1 binding) → onserver:message wires `JSON.parse(raw)` → `handler(msg)` into the server `message()`; onclient:open/close/error wire to client `ws.on{open,close,error}`. **(2b)** new `collectChannelAttrHandlerNames(nodes)` → `{onclient, onserver}` sets; `route-inference.ts` gains a `channel-ws-handler` escalation reason + `FunctionRoute.isChannelWsHandler` flag: onclient handlers SKIP Trigger-7 → stay CLIENT (§38.10 wins over §12.2 Trigger-7, normatively per §38.10.2 — agent confirmed not ambiguous, no STOP); onserver handlers force-escalate but emit as plain callable server functions (`emit-server.ts`) with the dead HTTP route + client fetch stub suppressed (`emit-functions.ts`). Normal channel publishers (form `onsubmit=postUpdate(...)`) KEEP their route+fetch (not over-suppressed). **(2c)** `makeCallAttr` test helper migrated to real `call-ref` + 6 real-source `compileScrml→emit` canary tests (§28) — closes the S138 synthesized-AST-masks-real-source canary. PA-independent R26 (board + m-handlers): server `message()` binds `const msg = d; handleUpdate(msg)`; client `_ws.onopen/onclose` call onConnected/onDisconnected LOCALLY; onclient fns have 0 server routes + 0 fetch-stubs; `node --check` clean. +11 tests; full suite 23,946→23,957/0. **RESIDUAL → see `g-channel-onserver-cell-read` (NEW, below):** an onserver handler that READS a channel cell server-side is SPEC-silent (guarded against a compile/node-check crash, but a runtime `[...undefined]` is possible on the non-canonical read pattern).

---

### G-CHANNEL-ONSERVER-CELL-READ — an `onserver:*` handler that READS a channel cell server-side is SPEC-silent → compiles clean but can runtime-throw (no server-authoritative cell store per §38.4) — `RESOLVED S189 (E-CHANNEL-SERVER-CELL-READ, RULING A — folded into g-channel-publisher-server-cell-read arc)`
<!-- @gap id=g-channel-onserver-cell-read sev=MED status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S186 by the `g-channel-handler-wiring` fix dispatch (agent `a06f1df4c51155e5e`), not yet closed.** After onserver:* handlers were correctly wired into the WS `message()` path (§38.6.1), a handler body that READS a channel-declared cell server-side — e.g. `onserver:message=handleUpdate(msg)` where `function handleUpdate(msg) { @updates = [...@updates, msg] }` — lowers the `@updates` read to `_scrml_body["updates"]`. But the WS message path has NO HTTP request body, and §38.4 defines channel state as **client-held + `__sync`-wired**, with NO server-authoritative cell store. So the read has no defined value server-side. The agent guarded it with `const _scrml_body = {};` (so no ReferenceError + `node --check` passes), but `[...undefined]` would THROW at runtime. **The SPEC-canonical §38.6.1 form is fully correct** (the handler broadcasts from the parsed `msg`, does not read a cell) — this only bites the NON-canonical "read a channel cell inside an onserver handler" pattern (which the S186 dog-food board happened to use). **Classification (don't-soft-classify):** compiles clean + node-checks clean but runtime-throws with no diagnostic = the silent-crash class → MED. **Design ruling needed (SPEC-silent):** should an onserver handler reading a channel cell (a) fire a compile diagnostic (`E-CHANNEL-…` "onserver handlers cannot read client-held channel cells; broadcast from the message payload per §38.6.1"); (b) be DEFINED (give the server a synced cell mirror — a bigger §38.4 model change); or (c) stay UB-but-documented? Recommend (a) — a clear compile error steering to the §38.6.1 broadcast form — pending a user/SPEC ruling. Repro: `/tmp/df-channels/dispatch-board.scrml` (`handleUpdate(msg){ @updates = [...@updates, msg] }`). Cross-ref `g-channel-handler-wiring` (RESOLVED — the wiring this residual rode in on).

---

### G-CHANNEL-PUBLISHER-SERVER-CELL-READ — the CANONICAL channel publisher idiom (`@channelCell = [...@channelCell, x]`, PRIMER §9.1) crashes server-side: a server-escalated publisher reads the channel cell from an EMPTY request body → `[...undefined]` runtime throw — `RESOLVED S189 (RULING A — drop Trigger 7a + E-CHANNEL-SERVER-CELL-READ)`
<!-- @gap id=g-channel-publisher-server-cell-read sev=HIGH status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S189 while scoping `g-channel-onserver-cell-read` (verify-all-the-way-down per the S188 disambiguation lesson).** The filed onserver gap framed itself as "only the NON-canonical onserver-handler-reads-a-cell pattern bites; the canonical publisher form is correct." **That premise is WRONG.** The CANONICAL channel publisher idiom — `function postMessage(...) { @messages = [...@messages, x] }` (PRIMER §9.1, the documented flagship channel pattern) — ALSO crashes server-side, for the SAME root, more seriously.

**Root (empirically confirmed, 3 sources).** A channel publisher that writes a channel cell escalates to a server fn (§12.2 **Trigger 7**, channel-cell-write / broadcast — landed S180). The escalated server fn lowers the channel-cell READ inside the read-modify-write to `_scrml_body["<cell>"]`. But the client fetch stub serializes only the fn ARGS into the request body — NEVER the channel cell (§38.4: channel state is client-held; there is NO server-authoritative cell store). So `_scrml_body["<cell>"]` is **undefined** server-side, and `[...undefined, x]` throws `TypeError: undefined is not iterable` at runtime on first publish. Compiles clean, `node --check` clean, NO diagnostic.

**Empirical (verify-before-claim):**
- `examples/15-channel-chat.scrml` (the CANONICAL channel example) → `server.js`: `broadcast({ __type: "__sync", __key: "messages", __val: ([..._scrml_body["messages"], {...}]) })` — `_scrml_body` has only `{author, body}`; `["messages"]` undefined → crash.
- `examples/23-trucking-dispatch/channels/dispatch-board.scrml` (the FLAGSHIP app) → `[..._scrml_body["boardEvents"], {...}]` — same crash.
- `/tmp/df-channels/dispatch-board.scrml` (the onserver-gap repro) → `postUpdate` (publisher, line 47) AND `handleUpdate` (onserver, line 77) BOTH crash. (`examples/08-chat.scrml` is NOT affected — its `@messages` is a plain reactive cell, NOT a channel cell, so the append runs client-side.)

**Classification (don't-soft-classify):** silent-compile + node-check-clean + runtime-throw on the CANONICAL idiom of a shipped flagship feature, affecting the canonical example + the flagship app → **HIGH**. Context the user should weight: channels are an unverified-end-to-end surface (no `VERIFIED.md` entry; examples need a running server) + no current adopters — so it is a LATENT high, not a live-user regression. But the severity of the defect itself is HIGH per the rule.

**This couples to `g-channel-onserver-cell-read` (the (a) ruling) through the §38.4 model — needs a UNIFIED model ruling before either is fixed.** The fork:
- **(A) Keep "no server channel store" (the (a)-onserver model) + fix the publisher to NOT round-trip the cell-read through the server.** Direction: a function whose only server-needing-reason is a channel-cell WRITE should keep the cell write CLIENT-side (the client has the cell → mutate locally → `__sync` broadcast relays it; the server is a dumb relay per `server.js` message() `if (d.__type === "__sync") { ws.publish(...); return }`). This RE-EXAMINES §12.2 Trigger 7a (S180): channel-cell-WRITE may NOT warrant server escalation (only `broadcast()`/`disconnect()` — Trigger 7b — genuinely need the server hub). Under (A), the onserver (a) diagnostic stands (onserver handlers run purely server-side, never have the cell). **PA lean.**
- **(B) Server-authoritative channel mirror** (the heavy §38.4 change): give the server channel state. Then BOTH publisher read-modify-write AND onserver reads become DEFINED → the (a) onserver diagnostic becomes WRONG. Bigger model change; contradicts client-held.
- **(C) Client threads the cell value into the publisher request body** — wasteful (ships the whole array each call), and onserver handlers (no client request) still can't → keeps (a). Middle option.

**Fix loci (for whichever direction):** `compiler/src/route-inference.ts` (Trigger 7 `detectChannelBroadcastReason` / channel-cell-write escalation), `compiler/src/codegen/emit-channel.ts` (publisher lowering), `compiler/src/codegen/emit-server.ts` / `emit-functions.ts` (the `_scrml_body[cell]` read lowering). SPEC §38.4 / §12.2 Trigger 7 / §38.6. Repros above. Cross-ref [[g-channel-onserver-cell-read]] (the coupled onserver instance — same root).

**RESOLVED S189 (RULING A, change-id `channel-cell-write-client-side-A-2026-06-12`; user ruled A = "keep client-held, re-examine Trigger 7a"; dispatched to `scrml-js-codegen-engineer` which CRASHED mid-Part-2 [socket error, 86 tool-uses], PA-recovered + finished + landed). Closes BOTH this HIGH and [[g-channel-onserver-cell-read]] (MED) — same root.** **Part 1** — SPEC §12.2 Trigger 7 amended: sub-clause (a) channel-cell-WRITE escalation DROPPED (a cell-write is a CLIENT-side sync-emit via `syncShared`/`__sync` §38.4/§38.7, proven by the onclient Bug-2b path §38.10; not a server-placement signal); only (b) `broadcast()`/`disconnect()` remain (Trigger 7b). `route-inference.ts detectChannelBroadcastReason` drops the cell-write reason. Result: every corpus channel publisher (pure cell-write, zero `.scrml` migration) now emits CLIENT-side. **Part 2** — NEW Error `E-CHANNEL-SERVER-CELL-READ` (§34 + §38.6.1): a SERVER-context channel function (onserver:* handler / `broadcast`/`disconnect`/SQL-escalated) reading a channel cell is rejected (client-held, no server value); `detectServerContextChannelCellRead` walker in route-inference. **Minimal-A ruling (user S189 "land min A"):** a deprecated `server function` channel-cell-write publisher is NOT auto-migrated — the `server` is now load-bearing (migration keeps it), and the server-side cell READ fires E-CHANNEL-SERVER-CELL-READ steering the author to drop `server` → client by hand. **Crash-recovery:** Part 1 was committed on the dead branch (`2f678c81`) + R26-verified; Part 2 salvaged from the worktree working-tree; PA re-applied + reconciled 3 old-model migration/MCP tests (all the deprecated `server function` channel-publisher shape) + added the Part-2 diagnostic tests. **PA-independent R26 (S138):** 15-channel-chat + trucking publishers → client-side (`_scrml_reactive_set` + `syncShared`, no `_scrml_body[cell]`, `node --check` clean); onserver-read + broadcast-read → E-CHANNEL-SERVER-CELL-READ fires; pure-client-publisher + broadcast-no-read → no false fire. Full pre-commit subset 16,829/0. Follow-up filed: [[g-channel-server-keyword-auto-migrate]] (Enhanced-A — teach the migration to auto-strip a pure-cell-write `server function` channel publisher → client; deferred, zero corpus demand).

---

### G-CHANNEL-SERVER-KEYWORD-AUTO-MIGRATE — `bun scrml migrate` does not auto-strip a deprecated `server function` channel-cell-write publisher → client under RULING A (it fires E-CHANNEL-SERVER-CELL-READ + leaves it for manual fix) — `NEW S189; LOW; migration ergonomics (Enhanced-A deferred)`
<!-- @gap id=g-channel-server-keyword-auto-migrate sev=LOW status=open -->

**Filed S189 as the deferred Enhanced-A half of [[g-channel-publisher-server-cell-read]] (the user ruled "land min A").** Under RULING A (S189), a channel-cell WRITE is a CLIENT-side operation (Trigger 7a dropped). The `server`-keyword migration (`rewriteServerFunctionKeyword`, S180) strips `server` only where it is *redundant* (the function escalates anyway). A deprecated `server function` channel publisher that ONLY writes a channel cell does NOT self-escalate under A → `server` is load-bearing → the migration KEEPS it. The author is instead steered by the new `E-CHANNEL-SERVER-CELL-READ` hard error (the server-side cell read) to drop `server` → client by hand. **Enhanced-A would** teach the migration (+ the `W-DEPRECATED-SERVER-MODIFIER` lint fire conditions) to recognize a pure-cell-write `server function` channel publisher as "belongs on the client under A" → auto-strip `server` → client (smoother UX; no hard error). **Severity LOW** — ZERO corpus demand (no real app has a `server function` channel publisher; all corpus publishers are the canonical no-`server` form, already client-side per Part 1); the minimal-A diagnostic is a clear, guided fix. **Re-trigger:** an adopter reports friction migrating a legacy `server function` channel publisher, OR a corpus `server function` channel publisher appears. **Fix loci:** `compiler/src/commands/migrate.js rewriteServerFunctionKeyword` (the redundancy/strip decision) + the `W-DEPRECATED-SERVER-MODIFIER` fire conditions (route-inference / type-system) — recognize channel-cell-write publishers as strip-to-client.

### G-CHANNEL-SPEC-38-9-STALE — §38.9 error-code table + §38.2/§38.3.1 bare-vs-quoted reconnect are SPEC-internally inconsistent post-v0.3-reversal — `RESOLVED S189 (PA-direct doc-currency)`
<!-- @gap id=g-channel-spec-38-9-stale sev=LOW status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S186 dog-food (channels §38).** SPEC-internal inconsistency (a doc bug, not spec-vs-impl): (1) §38.9's error-code table still lists `E-CHANNEL-INSIDE-PROGRAM` as the live placement error ("`<channel>` appears as a descendant of `<program>` rather than at file top level — D3/M19") and OMITS `E-CHANNEL-OUTSIDE-PROGRAM` + `E-CHANNEL-INSIDE-PAGE` — directly contradicting §38.1 / §38.4.1, where the v0.3 reversal (2026-05-12) made channel-inside-`<program>` CANONICAL and explicitly RETIRED `E-CHANNEL-INSIDE-PROGRAM` ("its trigger shape is now canonical, not violating"). The §38.9 table was never updated for the reversal. (2) §38.3.1's `channel-reconnect` worked examples show the QUOTED form (`"500"` / `"5000"`) while §38.2's `<channel reconnect=2000>` is BARE — pick one canonical reconnect form (ties to g-channel-reconnect-bare-int's disposition: once bare is accepted, make §38.3.1's examples bare or note both-accepted). **Verified-not-a-compiler-bug (companion finding):** the placement WALKER itself was correctly updated for v0.3 — channel-inside-`<program>` compiles clean (E-CHANNEL-INSIDE-PROGRAM does NOT fire); only the §38.9 doc table lags. (Separately, PRIMER §13.7 B19-specifics still describe the pre-v0.3 `walkChannelPlacement` firing E-CHANNEL-INSIDE-PROGRAM at depth≥1 — historically-frozen B19-landing prose; minor, fold into the SPEC-doc cleanup if convenient.) **Fix:** §38.9 table — retire the `E-CHANNEL-INSIDE-PROGRAM` row, add `E-CHANNEL-OUTSIDE-PROGRAM` + `E-CHANNEL-INSIDE-PAGE` rows (cross-ref §38.1/§38.4.1); §38.3.1 reconnect-form consistency. Naturally bundles with the g-channel-reconnect-bare-int / g-channel-handler-wiring landing as the SPEC-side cleanup.

**RESOLVED S189 (PA-direct, doc-currency only — no compiler source, no §34 code change).** All three parts: (1) §38.9 LOCAL error-table (SPEC ~line 18765) — retired the stale `E-CHANNEL-INSIDE-PROGRAM` row (struck-through + "Retired 2026-05-12 v0.3 Wave-1 reversal" note, mirroring the §34 catalog treatment) and added `E-CHANNEL-OUTSIDE-PROGRAM` + `E-CHANNEL-INSIDE-PAGE` rows (with the S87 module-file dispensation), reconciling §38.9 with the already-correct §34 catalog rows. (2) §38.3.1 reconnect "Accepted form" — de-quoted the `"500"`/`"5000"` illustration to bare `500`/`5000` (matching `<channel reconnect=N>` in §38.2 + the resolved g-channel-reconnect-bare-int), and clarified that the bare-integer form is canonical while the quoted form is reserved for unit-suffixed duration strings. (3) PRIMER §13.7 B19 row — added a v0.3-currency note flagging that the row records the pre-v0.3 landing and the walker now fires `E-CHANNEL-OUTSIDE-PROGRAM`. SPEC-INDEX Sections-table regenerated + footer re-synced (32,241→32,252, ~9 drift since S185) + section count corrected 58→59 (§59 landed S168, footer never updated). Net SPEC +2L.

### G-CHANNEL-TOPIC-FORWARD-REF — `<channel topic=@var>` fires E-SCOPE-001 when `@var` is declared AFTER the channel in source order (forward-ref doesn't hoist) — `RESOLVED S189 (preBindReactiveStateCells §6.9 hoist pre-pass — general, all attrs)`
<!-- @gap id=g-channel-topic-forward-ref sev=LOW status=resolved -->

**RESOLVED S189 (`g-channel-topic-forward-ref-2026-06-12`, agent `af9fe48c124dced27`, FINAL_SHA `2850bac5`, PA-landed via file-delta).** **Root = source-order-partial scope set, NOT the `@`-slice** (the `@@` tell was a red herring — reactive cells are dual-bound under `@name`/`name`, so `scopeChain.lookup("@selectedRoom")` works; the `@`-retention at `visitAttr` is intentional). The main `annotateNodes` top-level walk binds a cell into scope only when it REACHES that cell's `state-decl` — so an attribute `@`-ref whose markup node is visited BEFORE the decl saw an empty scope → false E-SCOPE-001. There was a file-scope pre-bind for exported names + engine auto-decls but NONE for plain reactive cells (§6.9 hoisting). **Fix:** new `preBindReactiveStateCells` pre-pass in `type-system.ts annotateNodes` (after `preBindExportedNames`) — seeds every file-scope reactive cell `asIs` (dual-bound `@name`/`name`) before the walk, with the `!scopeChain.lookup` guard (won't contest engine auto-decls / exported names → collision diagnostics still surface); the `asIs` seed never masks the resolved type (state-decl's "preserve prior richer type" guard); recurses container blocks but skips `function-decl` bodies (function-local, not file-scope). **General beyond channels:** the fix is at the hoisting layer → ANY attribute `@`-ref to a later-declared cell now resolves (channel `topic=`, generic `value=`, etc.) — the §6.9-conformant behavior, not channel-specific. **PA-independent R26 (S138):** AFTER (forward-ref) clean; BEFORE (back-ref) clean; GHOST (undeclared `@ghostRoom`) STILL fires E-SCOPE-001 (no over-suppression); generic non-channel attr forward-ref clean; bare-name missing-`@` (`value=laterCell`) still fires (F5 path intact). +7 regression tests. Full pre-commit subset 16,836/0.

**Surfaced S186 dog-food (channels §38, Tier-3 surface sweep).** The dynamic-topic form `<channel name="rooms" topic=@selectedRoom>` — the SPEC §38.2 / §38.6.2 canonical shape — fires `E-SCOPE-001` ("Unquoted identifier `@selectedRoom` in attribute `topic` … did you mean `@@selectedRoom`") when `@selectedRoom` is declared AFTER the channel in source order. **Pinned to pure source-order (not the `${}` wrapper):** cell declared BEFORE the channel (bare top-level OR in a `${}` block) → compiles clean; cell declared AFTER (bare OR in `${}`) → E-SCOPE-001. So the channel-attribute `@`-ref scope-check in the TS pass does NOT resolve against the full file-scope-hoisted cell set (cells SHOULD hoist per §6.9 hoisting model — a forward `@`-ref to a later-declared cell is legal elsewhere in the language). The `@@` double-sigil suggestion in the message is a tell that the base-name slice retains the leading `@` on the unresolved path. Same general region as `g-channel-reconnect-bare-int` (`type-system.ts visitAttr`, channel attrs routed through the generic markup-attr scope-check) but a DISTINCT mechanism (`@`-ref forward-ref hoisting, not bare-numeric-literal rejection). **Severity LOW** — natural workaround (declare channel state before the channel, as the canonical examples do); but it's an order-sensitivity that contradicts §6.9 hoisting and surprises. Likely extends to other channel `@`-bearing attrs (verify at fix time). **Fix:** ensure the channel-attribute `@`-ref scope-check resolves against the hoisted file-scope cell set (run after full cell registration, or treat channel-attr `@var` like any other hoisted reactive read). Repros: `/tmp/df-channels/x-topic-A.scrml` (after → fails) vs `x-topic-B.scrml` / `x-topic2.scrml` (before → clean). NOT bundled into the in-flight `channel-codegen-fixes-2026-06-12` dispatch (different root); separate follow-up.

---

### G-SCHEMAFOR-PA-UNRECOGNIZED — `schemaFor`-generated `<schema>` DDL is invisible to the protect-analyzer → false `E-PA-002` on the canonical §41.15 Form-B when no db file pre-exists — `RESOLVED S189 (PA-side Form-B recognition)`
<!-- @gap id=g-schemafor-pa-unrecognized sev=MED status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S186 dog-food (schema §39 / L22 `schemaFor`).** The canonical §41.15 Form-B usage — `<schema> ${ schemaFor(Driver) } </>` (the function-call form ratified at OQ-SCH-1; "define a struct → get the SQL schema without writing DDL") — fires `E-PA-002` ("Database file `…` does not exist and no CREATE TABLE statement was found … for table `drivers`") whenever the db file does NOT pre-exist (the common dev / first-run case). **Isolated (verify-before-claim):** a LITERAL `<schema> drivers { … } </>` block with the identical no-db-file setup compiles CLEAN — the protect-analyzer recognizes a literal `<schema>` table-block as a table-definition source (satisfying E-PA-002) but does NOT recognize a `schemaFor`-generated one. **Root (stage-ordering):** the protect-analyzer (`protect-analyzer.ts`, an early pipeline stage) scans for table-definition sources BEFORE the L22 `schemaFor` codegen expansion (`emit-schema-for.ts`, codegen stage); at PA time the `<schema>` body is still the unexpanded `${ schemaFor(Driver) }` interpolation, so PA sees no `drivers` table-block → E-PA-002. Table name is NOT the issue — `schemaFor` pluralizes per §41.15.2 (`Driver`→`drivers`), matching `<db tables="drivers">`; both the plural and singular `tables=` forms fire. **Severity MED** — it false-fires on the canonical Form-B of a SHIPPED flagship-adjacent L22 member (schemaFor, S104) and undercuts its whole value-prop (you still need the db file to pre-exist OR a literal CREATE TABLE in a `?{}`, defeating "no DDL"). Workaround: pre-create the db file, or use a literal `<schema>` block (but then schemaFor is pointless). **Fix direction:** teach the protect-analyzer to recognize a `${ schemaFor(StructType) }` interpolation inside `<schema>` as a table-definition source for the pluralized table name (resolve the struct + its §41.15.2 table name at PA time, without needing the full codegen expansion) — OR run the table-source-discovery after schemaFor expansion. Repros: `/tmp/df-schema/schemafor.scrml` + `sf2.scrml` (E-PA-002) vs `schema2.scrml` (literal `<schema>`, clean) — all with no db file present.

**RESOLVED S189 (`g-schemafor-pa-unrecognized-2026-06-12`, agent `aab252e80c605044c`, FINAL_SHA `13ea8e7e`, PA-landed via file-delta).** Fix locus = the brief's recommended PA-side recognition (no stage reorder). `protect-analyzer.ts` gains a FOURTH (lowest-precedence) ColumnDef source: `extractSchemaForCreateTableStatements` resolves `schemaFor` import-locals (alias-aware), builds a struct-name→raw registry from `type-decl` nodes (both available at the PA stage), walks `<schema>` block children for `schemaFor(Struct)` calls, pluralizes per §41.15.2 (local mirror with a keep-in-sync comment to `emit-schema-for.ts`), synthesizes a literal-`<schema>`-shaped body, and feeds it through the SAME `parseSchemaBlock` + `generateCreateTable` lowering as the literal path — so the shadow-DB columns are byte-consistent with the literal form, no schemaFor-codegen duplication. Lowest-precedence wire-in (`if (!createTableMap.has(tableKey))`) — never overrides a `?{}`-harvested or literal-`<schema>` table. Robust fall-through (unresolved struct / unparseable body / zero columns → skip → existing missing-table behavior). Guard `if (schemaForLocals.size === 0) return` so a user's own `schemaFor` (no `scrml:data` import) is not assumed ours. **PA-independent R26 (S138 dual-verify) at landing:** case 1 Form-B no-db → CLEAN (E-PA-002 gone); case 2 literal control → CLEAN (no regression); case 3 genuine-missing → E-PA-002 STILL fires; case 4 mismatch `schemaFor(Driver)` + `tables="ghosts"` → E-PA-002 fires precisely for `ghosts` (only `drivers` registered — no over-suppression). +158-line regression test (6/6). Pre-commit subset green.

---

### G-MARKUP-CONST-CONSUMES-CELL-DECL — a `<cell> = init` decl following a `const X = <markup>` inside a `${}` block isn't registered → `@cell` fires E-SCOPE-001 — `NEW S186; LOW; parser (markup-const body over-consumes)`
<!-- @gap id=g-markup-const-consumes-cell-decl sev=MED status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S186 dog-food (components/snippets §15/§16 sweep).** Inside a `${}` logic block, a markup-typed `const X = <markup>...</markup>` definition followed by a V5-strict structural cell decl (`<cell> = init`) causes the cell decl to be MIS-PARSED (consumed as markup continuation of the const's body) → the cell never registers at file scope → any later `@cell` reference fires `E-SCOPE-001` ("Unquoted identifier `@cell` … did you mean `@@cell`"). **Isolated (verify-before-claim), order-dependent:** `${ const G = <div…>…</div>; <name> = "Ada" }` → FAILS on `@name`; `${ <name> = "Ada"; const G = <div…>…</div> }` (cell FIRST) → CLEAN; `<name> = "Ada"` as a BARE top-level decl (no `${}` wrapper) + `const G = …` → CLEAN. So the trigger is precisely [markup-typed const, THEN structural cell] inside the SAME `${}` block — the markup-const's body parse doesn't terminate before the following structural decl and swallows it. **The `@@` double-sigil suggestion is the same cell-not-registered tell as `g-channel-topic-forward-ref` + the (resolved S185) validator-inline-colon cascade — a family of "cell registration silently corrupted → misleading E-SCOPE-001 on the cell" bugs.** **Severity LOW** — the canonical form is unaffected: PRIMER §6.4(5) declares `const Field = …` + `<userName> = …` as BARE top-level decls (and under v0.3 default-logic mode that's the non-redundant form; the `${}` wrapper itself fires `W-PROGRAM-REDUNDANT-LOGIC`). Workarounds: declare cells before the markup const, or don't wrap in `${}`. But it's a real parser registration bug (a cell in a `${}` block SHALL register per §6 — §38.1 even shows `${ <username> = "" }`), surprising, and shares the misleading-E-SCOPE-001 surface. **Fix direction:** the markup-typed-const body parser (ast-builder / block-splitter) must terminate the markup value at its closing tag and not consume a following sibling structural decl in the same logic block. Repros: `/tmp/df-sweep/c5.scrml` (const-then-cell → fails) vs `c6.scrml` (cell-then-const → clean) + `c4.scrml` (bare top-level → clean).

**S190 RE-TAG LOW→MED + symptom changed (verify-before-dispatch, PA-confirmed at HEAD `ea7eea43`).** S189's §6.9 `preBindReactiveStateCells` hoist (`type-system.ts:10589`) MASKED the loud `E-SCOPE-001` (it pre-binds file-scope reactive cells from existing `state-decl` nodes, so `@name` now resolves) **but did NOT fix the parse** — the markup-const body still swallows the trailing `<name> = "Ada"` decl's INITIALIZER, so the cell defaults to canonical-empty (`""`) and renders EMPTY instead of `"Ada"`. The bug went from LOUD (E-SCOPE-001) to SILENT (data loss): `"Ada"` appears NOWHERE in the emitted output, while the clean orderings (cell-first / bare-top-level) both emit `_scrml_reactive_set("name", "Ada")` + `_scrml_init_set("name", () => "Ada")`. Silent-wrong-output > loud-diagnostic → **re-tagged MED (user ruling S190)**; the original LOW rationale ("loud-not-silent") is now invalid. The fix must restore the FULL decl (name AND init) — NOT lean on the §6.9 hoist (it binds names only, cannot recover a lost initializer). DISPATCHED S190 with [[g-derived-rhs-interp-wrapped]] (same family, one dispatch) — `docs/changes/cluster-c-decl-boundary-mis-split-2026-06-13/`. Fresh repros: `/tmp/cc-s190/c5-const-then-cell.scrml` (+ c5b multi-cell / c5c nested-interp / c5d render-const — all silent-empty) vs c6/c4 (clean, "Ada" present).

**RESOLVED S190 (`cluster-c-decl-boundary-mis-split-2026-06-13`, agent `a3dc49d147e9cdfa5`, FINAL_SHA `39ae06ac`, PA-landed via file-delta).** Two-layer parse fix in `ast-builder.js` (no new code — making valid scrml parse). **Layer 1 (`collectExpr` markup-RHS boundary):** new `markupEverOpened`/`markupRootClosed`/`pendingRootCloseGt` tracking — once the top-level markup root of a `const Name = <markup>` / markup-typed-derived RHS fully closes (`</tag>`/`/>`/void-`>`, each deferred to the terminal `>`), `collectExpr` breaks BEFORE the next sibling instead of reading the trailing `>` as a binary operator and vacuuming the sibling into the const's raw body. **Layer 2 (defChildren vacuum):** `DEF_CHILD_STOP_KINDS` extended with `state-decl`/`function-decl`/`const-decl`/`let-decl` so a `component-def` no longer absorbs following file-scope decls into `defChildren` (SQL/CSS/markup siblings still attach — the collectexpr-blockref SQL-defChild contract preserved). **Plus** a latent pre-existing `</>` anonymous-closer DOUBLE-decrement (guarded via `lastTok.text !== "<"`) the new boundary EXPOSED (caused 22 transient test failures during dev; resolved). PA-independent R26 (S138 dual-verify): c5/p1/p3/p6/p7 → cells preserve inits (`_scrml_reactive_set("name","Ada")`, a=1/b=2/c=3); p2 → `fn label` defined+called (no E-SCOPE-001); p4 → `<userName/>` EXPANDS to `<input>`; c6/c4 controls clean; `node --check` all pass; full suite 24084/0. The broadened symptom matrix (cells/deriveds SILENT, bindable SILENT-literal, fn LOUD, even self-closing const bodies — surfaced by PA dog-food during the agent-wait) all closed. +19 regression tests (`cluster-c-decl-boundary.test.js`).

### G-NOT-NEGATION-UNENFORCED — `E-TYPE-045` (`not` used as boolean negation) is SPEC-`SHALL`-error but the compiler accepts it silently — `RESOLVED S188 (all positions incl. attr-bare fire E-TYPE-045)`
<!-- @gap id=g-not-negation-unenforced sev=MED status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S186 by the tutorial-staleness audit (`docs/audits/tutorial-staleness-audit-2026-06-12.md`, the §7 HIGH finding) + PA-confirmed.** SPEC §42.10 (line 21678/21684) is emphatic: *"`not` serves exactly one role — it is the absence value. It is NOT a boolean negation operator. The boolean negation operator in scrml is `!`. `!(a == b)` is valid. `not (a == b)` is NOT valid."* §34 + §42.10 catalog `E-TYPE-045` ("`not` used in prefix position as a boolean negation operator (`not (expr)`)", severity **Error**, "emitted at `compiler/src/type-system.ts:5556`"). **But the compiler does NOT fire it.** PA-confirmed (verify-before-claim): `not @loggedIn`, `not (@loggedIn)`, AND `not (@x == 1)` (the EXACT SPEC counter-example shape) all compile CLEAN — zero `E-TYPE-045`, zero diagnostic. So a SPEC-invalid boolean-negation use of `not` is silently accepted as if it were valid scrml. **Classification (don't-soft-classify):** the compiler accepting a form the SPEC says SHALL be an Error = a spec-vs-impl `SHALL`-divergence (same class as the S179 `g-fn-sql-unenforced` E-FN-001 / `g-route-arg-fn` E-ROUTE-003 finds — a SPEC-mandated error the type pass skips). MED (silent acceptance; no wrong-output per se, but it lets adopters write a SPEC-invalid form that reads as boolean-NOT, which then behaves as scrml's `not`-coercion rather than negation — a real semantic footgun, and it's WHY the tutorial drifted into teaching `not x` as canonical negation). **Fire site:** `type-system.ts:5556` (the catalog's own cited locus) — investigate why the existing E-TYPE-045 path doesn't trigger on these prefix-`not`-of-boolean-expr shapes (likely gated too narrowly, or the `not`-prefix expr never reaches the check). Repros: `/tmp/df-not/a.scrml` (`not @loggedIn`), `b.scrml` (`not (@loggedIn)`), `c.scrml` (`not (@x == 1)`) — all compile clean, all SHOULD fire E-TYPE-045. Pairs with the tutorial §7 remediation (the tutorial teaches the SPEC-invalid direction partly because the compiler never pushed back).


**S188 LANDING (`g-not-negation-enforce-2026-06-12`):** enforcement wired at the expression-parser lowering choke-point (`preprocessForAcorn` stamps `_notPrefixNegation` → `harvestNotPrefixNegation` TS-J emits E-TYPE-045, once per stamped node, span-deduped); coupled corpus migration of 62 forbidden sites → `!` across 35 files (flagship + examples + samples + auth template); SPEC §34/§42.10 broadened bare+paren/all-positions. The first landing (agent a2cd30a3, SHA 1d24f62) covered 5/6 positions; PA independent R26 (S138 dual-verify) caught a residual attr-value bare-`not` hole.

**S188 RESOLVED (follow-up, agent a409100175):** the residual hole is closed. **Root (empirically re-diagnosed — NOT the codegen `rewrite.ts` Locus-3 hypothesis):** bare prefix-`not` in an UNQUOTED attribute value was shredded UPSTREAM at the tokenizer (`tokenizer.ts` unquoted-value reader) — `if=not @y` tokenized as `ATTR_IDENT "not"` (the absence VALUE) plus a stray bareword attr `@y`, so `not @y` never reached `parseExprToNode` / never stamped `_notPrefixNegation` → harvest never fired. The paren form `if=(not @y)` already tokenized as `ATTR_EXPR` and routed through the choke-point, which is why h5 fired but h1/h6 did not. **Fix (single source of truth = the existing choke-point harvest, no second emit site):** (1) `tokenizer.ts` captures a bare `not <operand>` unquoted attr value as one `ATTR_EXPR` (`isPrefixNotOperandAhead` guard) → routes through `parseExprToNode` → stamps → harvest fires once (h1/h6/member); bare `if=not` with no operand stays `ATTR_IDENT` (valid absence value). (2) `ast-builder.js` (parseAttributes) fires E-TYPE-045 on the §5.5.2-malformed unquoted COMPOUND shred (`if=@x && not @y`, h2 — the leading stray `not`+operand pair), naming the real cause instead of only the misleading downstream E-SCOPE-001. **All 6 positions now fire E-TYPE-045 EXACTLY once** (h1/h2/h6 newly + h3/h4/h5/f1/f2 + if-stmt golden unchanged; no double-fire — harvest dedups by span). Valid forms unaffected: `if=not` (absence value), a literal `not=` attribute, `x is not`, `= not`, `return not`, regex/string/prose interiors. Test surface: `compiler/tests/unit/e-type-045-prefix-not-all-positions.test.js` (31 cases — the prior "attribute if= (bare)" case used the PAREN form, which is why the suite stayed green despite the hole; corrected + bare-attr/compound/single-fire/valid-attr cases added). Native parser (`compiler/native-parser/`) E-TYPE-045 emission remains DEFERRED to the ~v0.8 cutover (NotValue atom; `.scrml` mirrors feature-stale).
### G-DERIVED-RHS-INTERP-WRAPPED — `const <x> = ${expr}` drops the RHS → E-CODEGEN-INVALID-JS — `NEW S188 dog-food; LOW; codegen defect on a plausible decl shape`
<!-- @gap id=g-derived-rhs-interp-wrapped sev=LOW status=resolved -->

**Surfaced S188 dog-food (g-not-neg preserve-surface validation).** A derived-cell decl whose RHS is wrapped in a `${...}` logic block — `const <bad> = ${ @names.filter(n => n.length > 1) }` — drops the RHS entirely: codegen emits `const bad = ;` (empty initializer, invalid JS) and the filter expression leaks out as an orphaned statement. The compiler's self-parse-check catches it loudly (`E-CODEGEN-INVALID-JS` + "compiler defect, please report" — NOT a silent invalid-JS ship), but the user-facing outcome is a defect message instead of either unwrapping the `${}` or a clean diagnostic. **Isolated (verify-before-claim):** `const <bad> = ${ @names.filter(...) }` (block-wrapped RHS, NO regex/`not`) → FAILS (`/tmp/dfn/t3.scrml`); `const <bad> = @names.filter(...)` (plain expr RHS, same logic) → CLEAN (`t4`) — the trigger is the `${}` wrapper on the decl RHS, NOT the contents. Root: the block-splitter/ast-builder treats `${` as a block boundary, so `const <bad> =` gets an empty RHS and the `${...}` becomes a separate logic block. **Severity LOW** — the `${}` wrapper is already redundant at page-body level (`W-PROGRAM-REDUNDANT-LOGIC` teaches removing it); the canonical `const <x> = expr` form is unaffected; loud-not-silent. **Same family as [[g-markup-const-consumes-cell-decl]]** (the `${}`-boundary-in-decl mis-split class). **Fix direction:** recognize a `${...}`-wrapped RHS on a `const`/state decl as the decl's RHS (unwrap), OR emit a clean diagnostic ("derived RHS should not be `${}`-wrapped; remove the wrapper"). Repros: `/tmp/dfn/t3.scrml` (fails) vs `/tmp/dfn/t4.scrml` (clean).

**S190 RULING + reconfirm (verify-before-dispatch, PA-confirmed at HEAD `ea7eea43`).** User ruled **REJECT + clean diagnostic** (NOT unwrap) — one canonical form `const <x> = expr`; the `${}` wrapper at decl-RHS is non-canonical (consistent with S182/S183/S188 ERROR rulings on this silent/defect-accept class + limit-primitives). Live symptom shifted from the recorded `E-CODEGEN-INVALID-JS \`const bad = ;\`` to `E-SCOPE-001: Undeclared identifier \`$\`` (the orphaned `$` leaks out as a separate logic block) — same root. Fix = NEW §34 Error code fired cleanly at the decl-parse site (suppressing the misleading `$`-orphan cascade), steering to the bare-expr form. DISPATCHED S190 with [[g-markup-const-consumes-cell-decl]] (same family, one dispatch) — `docs/changes/cluster-c-decl-boundary-mis-split-2026-06-13/`. Fresh repros: `/tmp/cc-s190/t3-wrapped-rhs.scrml` (fails) vs `t4-plain-rhs.scrml` (clean).

**RESOLVED S190 (`cluster-c-decl-boundary-mis-split-2026-06-13`, agent `a3dc49d147e9cdfa5`, FINAL_SHA `39ae06ac`, PA-landed via file-delta).** NEW Error `E-DECL-RHS-INTERP-WRAPPED` (§34 + §6.2 "RHS is a bare expression" subsection). Fired in `ast-builder.js` `tryParseStructuralDecl` after `collectExpr`: a trimmed RHS that starts `${` and ends `}` is rejected (naming the cause + the bare-form fix) and RECOVERS by unwrapping the inner expr — suppressing the misleading orphan-`$` `E-SCOPE-001` cascade (the Error still fails compilation). Covers all three convergent forms — derived `const <x>`, plain `<x>`, typed `const <x>: T`. PA-independent R26: t3/p5a/p5b → E-DECL-RHS-INTERP-WRAPPED (no `$`-cascade); t4 plain-RHS control → clean. Spec-faithful per §6.2 (all RHS shapes are bare expressions) + limit-the-primitive (user ruling S190: reject, not unwrap-accept). +tests in `cluster-c-decl-boundary.test.js`.
